et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are detached, one should be careful with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healthy;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if you cut an artery thus far as you observe, hasten to stop it by cauterization, or fill the vein with vitriol and hold it in your hand so the blood is stanched;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this remedy present, place your finger on the vein so the blood is congealed, and raise the vein with cold water until the bleeding stops, and hold it steady as it is necessary;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and what is more moderate and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this trenchant cautery of two parts, but the trenchant should be well spaced to avoid longer lingering of the heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less of their warmth.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And you should have between the two cauteries a space of two fingers, and then when you have signed in the two joints, and you pass the burning iron so that it reaches just to the bone, and covers the vein in the two joints.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and let them be separated between the two parts of the body, because it is not customary to use this cautery everywhere in every part.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes fall down to the veins that are on the top of the chief part of the fire, and it does not benefit from a cure of medicine that one makes, and you see the face of the patient becoming red, and feel or sense a difficult walking as if of frenzies.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and on whom the oil is tense and moist so that the hairs of the papers are fallen, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the heat of the tears, thus it needs this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it "cure contuse", and it is that you make three equal incisions on the forehead of the patient who has this disease, so that the hairs grow evenly from the front, then make three equal slits on the forehead according to the length.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the slits be thus, cutting into the forehead downwards to the nose, and the others two as they meet the ribs above the papers, and beware of incising the arteries that are above the ribs on the papers.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and align your hand with the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and wrap it in cloths to suck out the blood, then apply the spatula, adapted to the shape of the two parts from which it is formed.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision which goes down to the temple up to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the crust which is between the two fissures to the whole syphac that is on the bone, then make another section from the mean incision up to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put the instrument called "cultellaire" in the first incision, it is very sharp on one side and soft on the other, not very sharp, and that's its form.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting tool sloping towards the airy flesh at the heart, and make the cutting smooth towards the bone, and cut as much as it reaches the middle seam.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut off the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision continues up to what opens into the bone, and then make another section in the mean fissure up to the other defect.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract the blood equally, and press out the bone for the blood taken.

dou reume des eulz	two edges of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When no vein is found with accustomed catarrh, and you see the eyes clouded and small, and to clear the view, and the burned papers;

de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	where grains, where beast, where stone of mine or similar thing as iron;

de la gresle	of the sprain
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times there come in papers from the eyes things that seem rough in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	the works are such:

des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When papers sprout hairs unnaturally besides their natural ones, and are wrapped up, if they harm the eyes, and bring about ways of diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albumin, so that it is due to the destruction of the eyes.

ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	where by fire cautery, or by medicines applied according to whether it is before or behind the cautery chapter, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by canes, according to what I will say.

puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part beneath the parchment, beneath the aligned hairs, all along the spatula, from the large lancet just to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and place beneath the parchment a small tent of cotton and drapery, then sign on the parchment a figure of an inch, as if the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevated on the parchment which is divided into toes.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if it happens that one has mastery of coping with a great quantity of the parchment according to what the parchment is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make all along the spatula on the two lines that you have signed, and begin from the large lancet just to the small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let it be one of the natural fissures near the hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the onion in one of the two angles of the tumor, then scrape thoroughly;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips at a seam of a needle with all the subtle thread of wool, and suck out the blood, and make a knot above the superficies of the threads on the two eyebrows to any glutinous things, if you want to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if it doesn't heal, then leave the seam and the threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without a seam of things that are dry and constricting, for the skin relives at the suddenness of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is murder (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you design the paper of a figure that is as much like the leaf of myrtle, as we have told, in three ounces according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply this which overcomes small equal forces similarly to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the thing is not even, take a needle or it has one thread, and put the end in the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put another thread from the large lantern, and the second thread from the small one, and assemble between your two threads evenly;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have told, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and heal it until it is healthy;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the parchment are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	so it is necessary that you use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of wounds is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you convert the parchment and make it according to what I have said, and then make two wounds by art, and two subtle threads as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut as two heads of two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly above what surpasses the parchment of the eye, and stretch the two wounds of the two parts forcibly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that is stretched will become numb and blacken and decay, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If he delays, if he has forces, then heal him as much as he is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sewn, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer puncture the hairs;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and it's the shape of the two canes that you will make according to this design, and according to this quantity of length and width;
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the operations are such that you take a subtle needle, and you pull the silk thread soft and subtle;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the heads and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm's width long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then order in the hunting another subtle thread of silk briefly, and tie the two heads of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient's head in your healthy one;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be beneath the sun so that the operations are declared, for it's a subtle and minor operation, then put the needle at the root of the hair implanted, and make it pierce the paper hastily as much as you draw it above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then shave the hair up to the wound, and put in the wound that hair, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then extract your hand so that the hairs grow outward from the entire wound onto the parchment with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not grow with it, then you will pull the wound back to the bottom of the entire thread that you have ordained there, so that the wound grows outward from the top and you see it by the sight of the eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you will pull the wound and the thread, and shut the eye and let it be shut for two or three days, until the hair takes root in its place and the flesh grows over.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, then accompany a long hair of natural whiskers, and be elevated with that one or you let it, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the rotting of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the porridge comes into the eye, if there are two manners:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a cut, or from a cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the work in this is that you split that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and bind it so that it may be healthy;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not suitable that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but I work with softening things, as with fenugrec.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose water or altee and flaxseed oil being cooked, and anointments of yaquilon melted in one of the oils, and I wrap a bandage, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care not to let it settle according to the form it had before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these treatments that we have mentioned are not forces that address this illness, so it does not return according to the form it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is beneath, truly called "axacrati", and is naturally accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds and fractures and cauterization and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and you insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left arm to the right, so that the thread passes through the head of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then the flesh is sewn on top over the entire needle, and the scalp is covered with a spatula-like instrument large.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the skin of the paper returns according to what it should be, that's good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If this doesn't happen, take the razor and put it in the seam, and turn the paper, and make two seams or stitches within the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the head of the two seams be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which is not "I griesche";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are adjusted from below, from what follows on the paper, then add the two separated parts, and sew with a thread of linen;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the treatment with those softening medications that we have mentioned, and with tinctures, until it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a seam or a stitch or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain seam below the hairs of the papers, and according to what is written before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then uncover between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to have ingenuity in all they can do to make it return to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patients themselves, according to what they require of work and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	you burn of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this joint has its main bond in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of the oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to put the point of a razor underneath the paper, and lift it up high;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and hold as pincers, until you grasp what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too dull, so that the patient cannot suffer from the spatula being too sharp and bleeding the oil;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision be such that you lightly scrape off the assembled (skin), so that the paper regains its natural shape.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it is healthy all assembled, and never again in the sharp bitter oil, and raises gentle warmth, and of cooling.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the paper and the oil a strip of linen, and put on the oil a moistened wool in abundance of egg whites.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use gentle cooling and soothing things until it be healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and resembles a hard thick skin, and another which is not nervous, but resembles a whitish moist congealed moisture, that when one touches it with iron and cuts it with pincers, if it cannot be.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and one and another similar thing starts towards the large armorer, and increases little by little until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts their head in a healthy position, then they open their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and hold the paper in your hand, then bend the finger as pinces of small doubling, and stretch it upwards;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert the hair of a horse, or of a cow, or of an ox, and pull it strongly;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and fix it in the finger, and pass it through the entire needle, and tie the finger with a thread and stretch it upwards, and strip all the hair from the side of the finger which follows the prick and the vein to the head, then cut the remaining part at the root of the arm, completely subtle and with small forces, and let the natural skin or arm, so that by the incision, the flow of tears does not come habitually;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail on the thumb alone hurts, and the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then the scab forms all over the spatula-like soft tissue from which it is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And beware that the spatula-like instrument does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the prunella is not perceived;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour into the oil a little of warm broth, and make a poultice of litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal those who need it as much as they should be healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot inject the needle, and the nails cannot enter, often a cure is achieved with this type of nail medicine;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and it grows as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, then open the oil of the patient, and take the lighter spatula-like instrument according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the ankle subtly, and if you see that it diminishes at no point and the reason presses on it, then distill from your mouth into the collier oil made of litargire and red dou, and stop up the oil just until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then restart the other work according to the same method, until it is completely restored.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, so that an abscess does not form, then heal it first, and cure the hot abscess as much as it is healthy, then recommence the work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh shows damage from the lamprey oil at night through great trouble, then suspend it on the ninth day, and take one part and not all, lest the course of the lampreys does not come to life;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill into the red collier oil which is made of litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	It is the eyes of certain men who never had red flesh, and they cover the plumule and hold steady on the papyrus and turn to the devil, and resemble a rose of balaust.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the operations are that the patient puts their head in a healthy position, then they open their eyes, and gather all those things which are conveniently adjacent to it, and hold them with strength;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first vein, and continue cutting to the resection just up to the end, and be careful that you do not blind the eye during the operation;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be spatula-like, which we have described in the incision of the ankle and with small forces where one opens the sepulcher, just as the form appears after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is opened, apply the oil of broiet or where you distill coliere rouge and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the eye a piece of cotton with albumen of egg, so that it may be assured against a hot abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it stays there, and the blood flows beneath, and you suspect an abscess forming beneath, let the eye be still and treat the abscess with soothing things that reduce the abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work so that it may be healthy, and thus you make a straight characteer in the eye by this likeness.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But always it is necessary that you adapt the treatment to each weak eye according to its natural condition;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental way, in work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works unless you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are red veins that are covered on the eye, and they take away its function and obscure the eye for many years.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary therefore at first that you examine the eye, in which it is, is strong, and there is no other illness besides the cataract.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then touches it in such a manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put their head in their healthy tone, then suspend those veins all around according to his wisdom, and let the subtle double onions be according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be treated with a ninth-degree cautery, in the fourth sign of the zodiac according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then one wraps the subtle veins strongly, and extracts the blood hour after hour, until you see removing the veins that are far from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and beware that you do not blind the eye at the points of the spatula, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you do not grasp further than those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red colour to corrupt what is still dirty within the eyeball.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are not able to collect all this in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and it is assured that there will be no hot abscess, then restart according to this method which is presented above so that it may be healthy.
et c’est li forme des forces:	and it's the form of the strengths:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat it with cautery and ardent medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healthy, if there is an engine in it that you divide above the abscess, where it must be drained, and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, if you take out all the instrument of which it is the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "asper chief", and it should be made of iron indeed at the chief edge, and it should be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put it on the level of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the limb with exciting medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the limbs are swollen, and the flesh is raw, and the body of the bowel is swollen, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not recover and is not apostemized, and bad accidents come, know that it is healthy;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this does not work, then there is another technique to bring the fistula back to the perforated nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with bitter medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the forestay according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be attenuated up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone of the armier, and stretch out your hand to the eye of the pouch, then turn the entire forestay until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by this, that is if he holds his hand under his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the level of dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh is reborn and hardened the limbs, thus goes the matter to the nail;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open all over, and it does not come to disturb the nose, nor diminish, so it is necessary that you read the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the sound, then apply ventouses or heating iron without piercing to suck, then put on the eye a linen cloth made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then hold the eye, and apply a dressing with bandages and drapels;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the way of the dressings is that you take dressings fairly soft, and fold each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then hold steady by placing a hard bandage above, and reapply the cups to suck out the noxious matter that causes fermentation.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the cups and keep the eye steady day and night, and if the ligatures are too loose, it is necessary that you tighten them strongly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the ligature after day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, it's good.
se ce non;	If not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reapply the plaster and the dressings and the ligature and the cups until he is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	because of the tearing of the web-like membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When cracks appear in the web-like membrane, then open, and issue forth like grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you have seen the copious flow, the operations are such that you insert a needle at the root of the affected part below, then insert another needle where it has the double filament from the part of the arm.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and have them pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then thread the double filament and tie a part of the tube around, and hold it well, then remove the needle and place it on the same moistened eye in abundance of egg whites;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it be until the threads dry with the egg whites, then heal the eye with comforting things until the wound is healthy;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and many times the wound is restrained by a circle of cloth, each part of it, until it is healthy.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes have great appearance, if they pierce with a subtle spatula which comes from the front of the eye, and corrects the moist albuginous and descends to the eyes, and enters thus quickly;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not other than a swelling that is assembled in the eye, appearing like a serpent descending, and it's not a real serpent;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take the head between your hands from both parts, and move it so that you see the swelling come to the surface before your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then be still, and do not move, and hold the light steady, and see the patient's things as they normally are;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not move below, know that it's a real serpent, and the descent of the swelling is not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and touch the cornified web at the point where the conjunctiva continues with the cornified web and the cornea, until the swelling subsides;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is dislocated, if it is distilled into the sharp warm honey-like mixture at midnight, or warm or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then let it be cured by another cure until it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	from the inflamations of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have already seen the similarities of the sharp points in the division, and this is what needs to be pierced;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if it opens according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy oil firmly and tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of the oil in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if the eyes are on the right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are on the right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the thickness of a ray in that whitish part of the eye at the lesser arm's joint, then apply the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand so much until it pierces into the whitish part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the forefront of the measure of the space which is from the pruning up to the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and it is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the cornual membrane, and then place the instrument where the water is, then press it down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Here is the translation:
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rest a little, and if the water rises the second way, place the strength with the instrument, and when it is thus fixed and does not rise, then extract almagda lightly by turning your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in water a small piece of gemstone, and lift up this eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the eye droplets or lane moistened with rose oil and abundant water, and bind with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Us, and those who are of our kind, put on common bruise with abundant water.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the maggots cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", whose shape is this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And prick then the conjunctiva slightly, and do not go too deep in the font, but make the subtle layer, then you apply alum, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work appearing to the patient the Dormiteur approaching, in which he sleeps on his back in the darkened room;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be warned of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then disengage him in the same darkened house, and test his vision, and make him see no things, and then put him back in bed until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not suitable that you do this in the hour of treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate it, because the water rises hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	abscesses come, which you dislocate before the seventh day, and address what soothes the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is appeased, if you dislodge the vein and put on its face a little roll to cover any day, and so be then in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then exits from the house little by little, and converts into its cases;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made ointment with almaga, which draws out water, but I never saw any of it in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of the forms of alumgada, because those who do not know them go astray;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be arranged properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And they are the head of water of this same subtlety, and the last in four angles aague.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	There never arise or are born various joined characters, so that there are some which seem like scorpions with many feet;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there is such a one where it has a flesh-colored encrusted chart, and if it has a soft bone-colored chart.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that case of those charts which is soft and not encrusted, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open their nostrils, and throw the onion at those charts, and treat them with fire;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then seize that which you can sustain in the subtle spatula on one side, as much as you know that this chart is completely ostensible.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, open everything to the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and do not surge above it, or abscess bursts, if you drain it as it is fitting;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize them until the blood is staunched and all the flesh is burnt, then pour in either oil or egg whites or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the egg whites do not work, and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healthy;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not pass as it should, know that there is a new flesh growing in the bone above, where the instruments cannot come to cut;
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is fitting that you put a thread of linen, somewhat thick, and sew with our hands, and have between each stitch of space a digit or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and place the patient's head on a thread of his own nail to purify it, and treat with aromatic herbs until he breathes through his nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times they do so to the child as to schools, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold one head that comes through the nose to one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth to the other hand, and know one after the other in being thus, as we who are in a thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this as much as you know that the nuts have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, suck out the blood, and soak the thread in Egyptian unguent, and put it back in the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put or apply a poultice of warm plants for some days until it is healthy, and if it needs medicine treatments, then use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the shape of the instrument for cleansing the head, where they distill oils and medicines or apply them.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it is of silver or copper, resembling a covered lamp, like a cane, and the conduits thus.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, make a closed cane, and it is the plain instruments for cleansing the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and hold the handle to the head to keep it in place when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease called "telul" nestles in the head, and grows and becomes large again, until it is seen clearly when looked at.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore it is necessary that you cut into the bone at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then apply the cauterizing instrument or the burning medicine.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and one delays coping as long as it is great, if you take warning if it is hard, of fixed color, of poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not let the iron touch more, for it is an enchanted abscess, because when one copes only once, great evil comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of fixed color, and you see that one can cope with it all, if you look at the patient and their sense of fear, and cure the limb of things that are dry and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is touched and wounded
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when continuations of solutions come into one of these cartilaginous passages, it profits little, because in some homes.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is necessary then to make an incision when it has come to nothing, if you look at whether the wound is fresh in all its blood.
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then adjust the two lips of a wound to a suture, then cure it until it is healthy;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrub all the parts of their heart until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a suture, and hold them in place, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and incense bruised.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another sudden plaster, and let it stick as long as it holds by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the bandage is that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the bandage of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Many men have had deep abscesses in their limbs, similar to grains of veins, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then it is necessary that you turn the limbs, and divide into each node, and take them as pincers and cut into each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the oil after the incision of glassy pitch, until the wound is stained;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the ointment of ash, and heal the limb of dry things as long as it becomes healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the decay of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there is swelling on the gums where it is pressed, which the old people call "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	it is necessary that you hold them as in tongs, and cut to its root, and let the blood or sap flow.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply on the limb a vitriol ointment, or other drying and constricting powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut a second time, and cauterize.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	the filthinesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they gather at the head of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and often are the black and yellowish-green teeth, as far as the decay reaches the gum, and are the foul-smelling teeth;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	it is necessary that you hold the patient between your hands, and their head be in your sanctum, and take out the teeth or the scurfy scales, so that nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make from the blackness and the greenness, and from the yellowness and other stains, so that they be worldly;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have everything taken out;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that teeth have need of various forms of instruments for extraction, according to what the work demonstrates, because the roots that one extracts from the teeth have other forms than those that one extracts between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others are prepared with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of his pain that you delay to handle it as much as you can, for one must not do it hastily.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance just up to then that one has no excuse to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to undergo treatment, it is necessary that you be certain of the pain caused by the teeth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and believes it is in a sound tooth, and makes them handle the good tooth.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and thus the pain does not depart from him for that, as long as the bad one is extracted, for we have already wanted to do it to these sound ones.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides, strongly to guard the gum from all parts.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then place your fingers or subtle pincers at the first little by little, so that it is well loosened, then you will firmly affix the pincers.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient be in its natural position between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part, and remove it as you did previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the teeth are pierced and gnawed, it is necessary that you fill them with cloths, where the perforations are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you hold it subtly in the tongs, so that it does not break while holding.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to work carefully around the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take care not to break it, and leave a part behind, and reveal to the patient through the malice of the larger root more great pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act thus like the ignorant surgeon, who in their haste and hardness often break the instrument, and do not amend what we have recounted.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but often they come through the observation of this great illness due to the roots that remain, or through the instrument that they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is decayed, if you wash the jaw with wine or with axle-tree and elder;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and we remove blood that comes, which often happens, if you apply the jaw with vitriol paste;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if it does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments, which one must use to extract teeth first, should be long and thin points and large handles, so they do not slip when you pull out the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large limbs so they do not bend in the drawing, and let them be of iron well made, and let them be toothed to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the pulling, it is necessary that you put on the jaw a moistened cotton cloth in butter I or II, as long as the jaws are softened, then you apply the clamps called "algefri", from which the head seems to be in the shape of a bird's beak;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they are then made thus as a file and it is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to issue from all these tongs, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh totally around the root, and you put the instrument which is called "althali", it is to know plainness, from which this is their form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break easily, and if its root grows through that, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, then aid yourself with all the instruments, from which the forms come here afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one aids with this instrument which has many grooves, from which it is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are presented in the arrangement of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, from which it is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many of these dense instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are certain diseases where the ancients did not teach about instruments because of the diversity of wounds; and it does not break in the thick cartilage or other bones, or it putrefies, if they seek the instruments that they need, which I have told you, and aid with gestures, from which this form comes:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let it be thick and holding well to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but can hold and remove.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the limb with suitable medications for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if you take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course, and the form is ugly, and especially in young women, if it is necessary that you know that the teeth are not after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot make it straight or limber:
adonques lou raie;	then the root;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument which has the form, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be of iron pointed in the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the jaw closes little by little every day due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file a part of the tooth as it is in its shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file with which one makes the needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and with a file or instrument he touches little by little and gently in many places, so that it does not move until it is straight.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the flat surface at the end has no roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, it is necessary to file the asperity until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth locks
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth falls out, whether by shock or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it because they fear it will fall out, and you treat them with medicines that constrict, and that is not worth it.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	it is necessary to hold them together with a thread of gold, because the silver thread turns green and decays, but the gold does not move at all.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be neither too large nor too small, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to realign the teeth, take the thread and double wire between the two healthy teeth, then place the heads between the bad teeth, if there is one or more, until you arrive at the sound tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then recommence the covering up to the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and steadily, so that it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and be your ligature at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the heads of the thread to a small nail, and assemble them, and place them between the sound tooth, and set it so that it does not touch the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it constricted as much as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the threads break, hold it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains and serves thus all its tension, and it is the form of the teeth and the shape of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and of the two muscles, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not interfere with it, for those who are not wise and suffer, and never make the form of a tooth of ivory, and put it in its place where the defect is, and hold it steady as we have said, and it remains and serves thus long tension.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of covering the lien of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never are these bonds that come from under the tongue or naturally, which you do not know thus.
