ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accidental wound swelling;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your healthy one, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then take the nervous cord as large, so that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is toughness or knot, and it is suddenly a wound, if you cut the uncinate and take as large the ligament.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and beware that the fissure is not too deep in front, because of the artery which is beneath.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done it, lift the level of warm water and of hazel, or of cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and tighten the patient's bandage every night, so that the wounds cannot suppurate.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if a flow of blood comes, then put on the wound a vitriol ointment.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the wound does not heal, then cauterize it with a slow-cautery fire, which is good for that.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then the treatment of another treatment as long as he is healthy,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see that it is of bad color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it declines to a whitish color, and there is moisture, then he throws in the onion, and makes a subtle spatula-like instrument, and delivers on one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if you do not find it in your work, then put on a vitriol plaster as long as it is stained, then return to your work as much as you can treat everything fully;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the lever of vinegar and of seat, and the treatment of other treatments as long as he is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes there come into the throat bulges that are called "goiters", and they are properly called II swelling, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, take heed:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is abscesses hard of small sense and of false color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, also for the ornamentation of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let them be until they are ripe, and then you will divide them, or they would break apart by themselves;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color round, and the root is subtle, then prepare the instrument for covering, but first look to see if the abscesses are calm and at peace.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and their head be in your healthy one, and open their mouth and take the surgeon's hands between theirs, and press the tongue underneath all the instrument, so that it is in the form.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or subtle iron, just as our cautery irons:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can't you press the tongue on all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if you take the onion and fix it in the handle, and pull strongly upwards more than you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull something from the tiles with, then shape it to the instrument, because of its form, which seems like a force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all the tips are curved, and one end to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cover it with tongs, so that it takes its form.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be cutting on one side, and named on the other side;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have shaped one of the handles, shape the other according to the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, hot and gentle, and if there is evacuation of blood, gargle the patient warmly, or use scorched pomgranates that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is stained;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then let the wound heal until it is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and often no abscesses grow in the throat except the two glands, if they gather together thus like the two glands unite.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was nestled deep in her throat, to be known as the small abscess of sense;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had almost completely closed off her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so elevated there that it had poured out two loads through the two nostrils of her nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then, and made an incision in one of the angles, then the flow of pus was released, and a large portion of bowel was freed.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I made another incision in the other passage of the nose, and I opened the mouth and pressed on the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After I burned the anvil in these abscesses, and I cauterized a part of it, and only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And then the woman's throat became constricted, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop cutting into that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscesses grew again, and filled the void that I had emptied, so much that it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I tricked her and cauterized inside her throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Then the swelling began to grow.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I left those areas, and only God knows what happened afterwards.
de l’uve	of the egg
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the humors descend to the vein, and it is inflamed and it is long, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is very large and round, it is called a "vein".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit at all, and you see that the hot abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, so it is necessary that you grasp it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one that is rounded and assembled, and is not lengthy;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is blood-red or of a dark purple color or black, so it is necessary that you avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned previously.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then prick the onion in the egg, and pull it from below, and grasp it with one of the two instruments that I have said for the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not remove more flesh than the excess which is beyond the natural terminus;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more, it grieves at the voice, and at the speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two gums, and cure it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about operating, it is necessary that you use judgment in the cautery of the senses, for fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of burning with fire is sharp and bitter.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head in your healthy one, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cauterization, and confines it with living water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using the application of this instrument, because it is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let there be on the head a lock of hair or where one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a comb, and put the instrument to all the medicine onto the wound;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should be seated on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth to the medicine placed within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the blister;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then put your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the eye, for a quantity of about half an hour, until you see the narcotics and the murmurations of the medicine are appeased;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into all the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton adheres to the eye;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterization is perfected, then let it dry, and wait after three or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have mastery of reapplying the cauterization of the medicine, so reapply it, and after cauterizing, suck in the cotton soaked in borax, and clean what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be raised from cold water, and let it be cured of garglings as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, nor the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take chamomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put it there, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot is well glued with strong earth, and in the pot has an instrument that is arranged in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And let it be of silver or copper, and let one of the heads be applied to the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, so that the eye is mortified;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the repeated recommendation, until the eye dries out, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make a fiercer fire than at the decline of an abscess's heat.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a candle and put in the patient's head a thread of egg white, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the egg white thread does not let the vapor pass into the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times one is hurt at the throat by a fishbone or some other thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you extract what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing clearly.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear to you and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance if he vomits the bitter thing
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	where the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and there is a thread on the sponge, and then it passes through;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, if it sticks, and then you will draw it forth;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out of what we have said, take the instrument of a probe in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can enter more lightly into the throat, and hold the head high and lifted;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all may come to harm, and do not push the bone within;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is necessary that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows when the thing is bitter;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If you burn with fire below, or if you pull it straight with all the instrument equally, so that it is straight.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the swelling of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No wound is medicated, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it does not benefit at all, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, so draw it out completely with the small hook, or with subtle tenaculas that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a curved hook, and put it in the throat of the patient, then pull out with the curve of the hook the iron hot instrument, and make it often happen.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you touch the patient's aquiline all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full sight of the cold water, and open the mouth, and let it swallow in sense, and move it to its hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if soon the wound feels the water, it scabs.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not scab as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with assafetida, at the instrument that I said in the fumigation of the urine;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall sooner.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take the pot where there are visible coals, and it should be covered with a pierced cover in the middle, and in that perforation should be the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you throw in the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane into his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just to the sanity;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the sanity will fall now, and if it does not fall, then recommence the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink any water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then the liver will be cleansed by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument is where one treats the vein, it is, when one can see it, similar to curved tongs entering into the gorge;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has resemblance to a bird's beak, and it has roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot release;
et vez ci la forme:	and see there the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the surgeons of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many similarities of abscesses are, according to what the remembrance comes here after one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners, one of which is in its own likeness, and according to what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is by the abscesses or where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come into joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce, as long as the swelling is mild according to its accomplishment;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, like abscesses that are on the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves them until they are ripe on the outside, perhaps if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is on a main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it becomes ripe, it will not injure the main limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	where it is at the foundation, if you pierce it in this way so that it becomes mature;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not necessary that you pierce the abscess without complete digestion, unless it is at the foundation, so that it does not putrefy within, and becomes long and fistulous;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the hour of perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to completion, and it is when the pain is appeased, and the departure from fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the debate and agreement of the head of the abscess, and other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make a seat for the perforation or more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens mouths;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be far from the long body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and veins and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no abundance.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases where they suffer, according to the affected limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, if it is worth more that you let the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you make a hole before that, the body will be elongated from the venom of it, and is full of much foulness;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they harden the lips and the depths of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are abscesses that are pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limbs need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you make small abscesses, small holes;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large holes, and many fissures according to the likeness of the greatness of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the head, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has thus become jaundiced like I am wrapped, and is numbed, then one must do thus as they do for bubbles:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such ones that are split into three angles, and if there are such ones that one covers thus like the leaf of myrtle, thus like abscesses of the loins;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such ones where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, thus like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has gathered great matter, and you pierce them, if you do not draw out all the matter at that hour, but rather draw out a part;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just until the next day, then draw out nothing further there.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this many times with great effort, so much that the belly becomes entirely swollen.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expert often kills the patient with the issue of the bowel, which by chance causes the death of the patient, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Examine carefully this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, suck out the pus, and look if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a plain ulcer, apply a dressing made of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many perforations, then you should put a dressing in each one so that they do not touch each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, then you should fill it with old cotton or a dressing made from linen threads without moisture, and bind it just to the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the treatment of the joint until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the shedding of blood occurs in your work, so apply cold and still water, and do not agitate the dressing, and place it on the wound, repeatedly cleaning it many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the blood circulation perseveres, they will receive good government and treatment, and the powders that I mentioned in my hands in this book, and if it is winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary to apply tents and warm drapplings soaked in wine and hot oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is summer, and the limbs are weary, then it is necessary to apply warm drapplings soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then dissolve the abscess and the swelling and the treatment, as it is necessary, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And it is necessary to recognize universally in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	where you have said how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and see here this chapter.
des soros	of ulcers
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the blood comes from small abscesses, and there are ways of our own that are in tiles, just like the juice of a gall, and much is similar to it.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such as those which have moisture, just like pores;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are ones that are hard and stone-like to the cutter, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the cutting are that you experience with every instrument that is called "intromission", because its shape comes from this, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they feel it by probing above the loin.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, it dries out completely, leaving behind no skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves nothing.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, with water and wine, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and clean what has remained of the pus.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then replace the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that there remains no pus.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound of pricking at this suitable time, so it may be healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscesses hold in a thick humor, then cut according to this form, far from the loincloth.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and you scrape the ulcers, and remove the scabs from all parts, and put all your treatment of drawing forth the humor from the hip where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery does you harm in opposition, then do what I have told you to do afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do for the abscess if it is porous, and on cutting and on healing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the porous and moist abscess, it is easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if there are none of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and it was one of these abscesses that I cut from the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess just like a sour, rough and white stone, and it could not be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had touched any of them, one would have made a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming to the head, because those that come to the head of children and roots of the ears, the opening should be made at the most dependent part, in order to issue the pus;
et les cure si com il covient.	and the treatment should be as it is suitable.
des scrophules	of the scabs
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Here is the translation:
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each swelling is properly inside its side, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the similarities of these swellings are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one where you see good disposition in the touch, and it is similar in color to the body, and changes from each part and is not airy as nerves of the neck nor in the artery, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is suitable that you cut it from above, and scrape each part, and stretch the two lips of the heart as onions, if you are skilled in this, as we have said about abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and burn a little and slowly, and be sure that you do not touch the nerve or the vein, and are not too hasty with the scalpel, lest the hands falter, and do not see too far ahead, so you do not cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to stop, then put into the wound a vitriol ointment, or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound still.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begin to puncture.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then seek with your finger if there remain small scripules, if you cut and mold them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrophula, it does not suit to cut that scrophula at its root, but rather tie it off with a strong double thread, and let it fall away by itself without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the dressing of old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then the treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there will be no more superfluity because of the greatness of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cut at the root of it, and draw out strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrophulae that hold a surplus, pierce them where they appear most tender;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce them thus as the one mentioned before, in a dependent manner, then I will treat them with ointment and similar things, so that they do not corrupt what remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then treat it with ointment inflamed with charcoal, until it be healthy.
de squinance	of bruising
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I did not see anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have a squint, it is necessary that the notch of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be examined;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one must not help by this, because all the veins and the arm of the patient are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the mandrels.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the arm, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut beneath three circles or four a small cut of the traverse, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the siphac, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and thus it is convenient for the section of the epiglottis that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are far from inquiry.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to the entire onion, then cuts the heart as far as it reaches the collarbone;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and clears the vessels of blood, if you do not see anything, and then touches the syphac, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the collarbone which jumps forth by the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leaves the wound open a little piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew all alone without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	One must not delay until the throat is entirely obstructed, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then touches the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and therefore they command the old one to leave the open wound as long as the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four And then they command to cauterize the wound and cure, until it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took the needle, and she stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the sinew of her arm;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and I found her almost dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and saw well that it had not been properly covered, nor did a vein flow further than the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and cured it until she was healthy;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and I had not seen the young woman feverish when her voice was hoarse, and she returned afterwards to her usual disposition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I said that in the surgery of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This posteme is called " Hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of a jaundice, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	where nature has no point of obstruction.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which is similar to a fatty swelling, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not want to open or make fierce efforts except in the one that is small, and it proves and searches everywhere for the entire interior;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it thus as I do not find fat, and it does not penetrate to any vein, if it bursts, if one bursts as we do, and it draws out all its filth, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well everywhere, and the doctor if it suits him, so that he may be perfectly healthy.
des nous	of the nouns
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of our own, which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it suits that I say all the difference that is between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that the patient is feverish and tense, until the inflammation has passed, and the corruption is accomplished;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then replace the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new wound there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins thus like a abscess, and grows large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their similarities, whether gray, or moist, and many colors are thus as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the wound, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to what its shape will be or the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into the abscesses of the nails is that you grasp or touch the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, so that you feel that the struments have pierced the heart, then it is according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the suppurating matter, and take care in this that it bursts forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the running moisture is warm, whatever its color may be, thus do as I have said about the other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and after the suppurating matter has come out, know that it is fat, thus do it in a cross, and take it with pincers, and lightly scrape each part and turn the skin where it lies so that you draw it forth whole with the nail;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it forth whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if it stays nothing, it returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it stays a little, and the wound does not grieve, then apply to the wound some corrosive powders, and hold the wound steady, and put on soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and treat other wounds until they are healthy;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat what injures flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is beating against you or otherwise, then hasten and apply the liquid of broken vitriol, and let it stay two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and restore the ebullition of blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to the treatment that was left undone from the beginning.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of inward-turned instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	big and mild and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three kinds that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	big, mild, and small, to encircle the abscesses of a fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews up wounds, and they are of citrin tin, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more proven for sewing up black pustules;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	big, mild, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the onions are very similar, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	big, mild, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are wounds that have three kinds of curvature thus;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are wounds that have three curvatures, and are thus of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are wounds that have two curvatures, and wounds with a single curvature only, and are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is where they are cutting, and of such there are those that do not cut except in one part, from which one scrapes the nails, because one does not touch the vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introductions are the swollen limbs placed in shackles, so that the patient does not perceive themselves at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and moderate, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not make more use of it than in the charcoal burned flesh, if like legs, and arms, and limbs, and fingers, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and one does not make another small instrument, similar to the scrapings of fistules, according to this form, where one stains blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the body that is connected to the gathering of veins, and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	One does not inflate the limbs of certain men when they begin to be corrupted, as much as they seem like feminine limbs;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain worn out and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form of this line, up to G:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and apply the medicinal plaster in the open wound, then bring together the two lips of the wound to suture, and cure until it is healthy;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the limb falls downwards, and is amazed by its greatness like they have in women, if it makes two ribs above, through two similar fractures;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	of the one being held to the other at the end of the one and of the other, so that the larger line includes the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and prepare what we have said about bandages and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, so that it may be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healthy, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it be until it eats away the remaining flesh and fat, then cure until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the seats
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that form under the seats are kinds of hard scrofula sores where there are ribs, and if there is only moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture need to be treated according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire tumor that is in the abscess is evacuated, then fill the wound with much cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and cure by applying ointment to the extent that it becomes healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, then they do as we have said in cases of scrofula, and if the wound is open, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin that is above it is swollen, then many abscesses come from it, and just so does it happen to the inflamed and abscessed vein;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if you recognize it by its signs as it is for the artery, then are the long abscesses deep in.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel the strangeness;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, then are the veins devoid of apparent function;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, and similarly when it is under the seats and in the corners and in the hollow of the shoulder and many other places, and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary then to choose the iron cure, and he who is at the head must choose also, and in he who is inflamed with arterial fire it makes a hole above the skin of the loin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate on the incision like a wound, and beautifully separate the artery from the tiles, until it is discovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then stick the needle underneath, and make it pierce just to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread in two eyes, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then puncture the abscess which is between the two lines of an introjected foreign body as much as the blood that comes out of it, and so be freed from the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then proceed with the treatment that soothes the bowel, until the swelling subsides;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal the wound of the eye socket, arriving at that, until it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is of the size of a vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then stick the needle underneath where you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have a double thread, so that you draw from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then touch the abscess, as I have told you, or bind one of the two parts with a thread as the head of the vein.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread does not come out, then I rebury another needle under all the thread beneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut into the abscess until the superficies emerge, then cut into the superficial part of the heart and let what is bound go.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a dressing of soft cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply gentle treatments of poultices and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, how abscesses come into the arteries and veins, they come into the kidneys when they are fermented, or by too great a labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And it happens more often with joints and fingers in all places where there are joints, and this is the grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one extracts it forcibly, the patient feels pain, and it is not at all in the deep part of the body, but beneath the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it must be well adjusted on all parts, and does not move forward or backward, neither below nor above, and the one that is in joints does not need to be strengthened with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	perhaps they will encounter contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are at the head or forehead, make the skin on the spatula-like.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscesses are small, you hold them with pincers, and cut at their root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, you suspend it with an onion, and scrape it, then bone and assemble the wound to the sutures, and treat until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of the large hanging lumps
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	It sometimes happens in the belly and not another part of the body, and it is a disease which is called "fungus" by the resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots, and large lumps.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are small and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw some that had II or belly wounds that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and they were split open, and immediately corroded with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6 ounces, and the work in the incision is such that you observe if the patient's moisture is moist, and the color of the joint is pale and moist and with a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if you touch the spatula to the large one, and be in its presence with the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when you cut too deeply, there often come great flows of blood, and if the wound does not close, then hasten to give a cauterization.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of the iron, take the well-made thread of steel, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then hold it back, and do not cease from constricting the thread of steel until it touches the artery, and cut through it without strain;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, you should fear to cope with them suddenly through the belly, but you can well cope with most of it, then cauterize so they do not return;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cure the wound, and beware that you do not touch the ulcer that is of foul color and of poor sense and of lazy regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of encrusted chancre afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of a wound or fracture of the syphac, and it is on the belly and in some of the bouez, just as it happens in other ruptures, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and it is through the rupture of the skin and the issuing of the bowel, if it is the color of the abscess similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open to various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the outlet of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses on it with their fingers if it recedes, and then returns, and by chance if it is constricted, and greatly increases at the entrance of the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press on it with your hand, it does not constrain at all;
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is due to blood, it opens through these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the toucher, and the operations are that you examine whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter about abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his belly, and be straightened out entirely, then sign from the navel all around the abdomen.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command him to sit between your hands, then go into the place that you have signed to all the spatula-like, then is the majority of the abscess above all the large groin.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then bind him with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk, firmly, and be the nails that hold the dislocated limb.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open the majority of the abscess extended on the limb, and you thrust your index finger, and seek the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find the limb taken by the dislocation, so dislocate it, and thrust the intestine to the depth of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the bowel, take it by the navel, and cut off the superfluity.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery does contrary, or the vein, then go gently inside, then return to your work and take two needles, and thrust two strong threads, and thrust the two needles into what you have done in a cross that you make pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and let the limb relax as much as it can, and separate the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	where you find it when it is subtle and porous, then heal what needs to be healed, and shave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then heal the limb of what needs to be healed, and sew the limb.
dou chancre	because of a tumor
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken in the division about the similarities of cancer, and how one should operate with medicines, and how one should avoid the treatment with iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that cancer is engendered in the marrow, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when cancer is in the limb or where one can reach it if it is like cancer which is in the breasts, and in the hips, and in similar places, and it must be entirely removed when it is in its beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, you must not approach it, for I do not know how to heal any of them;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	I never healed any of them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the treatments, when it is in its place or where you can open it, as we have said, is that you should purge the patient of black bile several times;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him healthier if he has shown repletion, then prepare the patient in a good place to perform the treatment;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then cut your onions or cancels, and shave all parts, and scrape all parts without leaving anything;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and press well the place with your hand or anything, and if the blood flows back to you in opposition to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize until the blood is stanched;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of another treatment until he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of the water is done, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment which is done by medications, and that which is cured by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is suddenly inflamed;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	it is to know, tympanitis and hipsarca, for it is deadly things;
