donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the treatment does not benefit, if you see that the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as a tumor and solution of stomach and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if one should not touch with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient has a strong vitality, and he has no other illness but only dropsy, and it is not too young nor too old, then you should operate thusly:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lift the patient's right hand on your hands, and the assistants press the belly in bulging out the water at the lowest part of the thigh, then take the spine scraper in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	to a point, and so that it is not inserted too far in that it can come just up to the intestine when one fixes it in, and does not make it burst;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then see if the dropsy is advancing towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you make an incision below the belly, and you must direct the needle right down to the groin;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then make your incision on the left side of the belly;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is because of weakness, let it be to the right, and it does not seem that the patient should lean on the crack that the excesses do not run to the weak spot;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and prick, and lift your hand at all the spatium between the skin and the underlying flesh, as if scraping out the quantity of an ounce or so;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the underlying flesh until the spatium reaches the empty space, and it is the veins of the water, then pull strongly, and you prick this instrument according to its shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a subtle silver tube, and it is of silver or lighter arching, and has at the back part a small hole;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and where it is narrowed on one side, it has three holes;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and one from another part, and one from another;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut like a quill, and it's the shape of the incision that the writers cut with the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top is the scalpel, so that when the instruments come to the water, they descend now onto the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty the quarter or third part, for if you empty more than it is necessary at that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit of the arm, or he falls faint, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then pull the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held back now by the cord that stops up the passage which is on the syphac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then recommend the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw out a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do nothing for a day, and keep him from moving too much but only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you let him have much water, if the treatment of the grave wound or sore is hot, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and refrain from drinking.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the treatment with drying medicines so that it be healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the stopping of the flow
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never is a child born who does not have smallpox on the rod, or the smallpox is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If you want to make it so that it does not perceive at all the spatiumile, a very subtle mole according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put or insert a subtle cloth of fleece, and bind it thus for three days or four and when he wants to make urine, let the cloth be removed, and make him urinate, and then replace it.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance it does not converge at all points, for the urine that comes out does not allow it to close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	This is where the perforation is small, if it is medicated with a cloth of cotton, as we have said, it will enlarge itself.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the hole in their back are blocked, for none are born with a hole at the head of the penis, because they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up high;
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come up to the marrow, and it's a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the surgery is that the patients place themselves thus on their back, then they hold the head of the penis and the cope as wide as a penny, so that the hole appears in the middle, just as it converges;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the flow of blood that comes many times, and if it happens, then staunch what is bleeding blood, and heal the wound until it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	the blisters on the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times they come to this bath, and it is a false appearance of a wounded hand;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and non-malignant ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	it is necessary that you take them with the subtle onion, and clean and wash all, then put on cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with ointment diafinicon until it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and stinking, it is necessary that you apply fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cleaned it, and the bath is in a state of putrefaction, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the bath that is inside first;
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is soothed, then heal what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat them together, it is not assured that the head of the wound will not be perceived, and there comes darkness and corruption in the wound and in its junction;
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes, then apply the lunar cautery in this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery fires help with these two conditions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	it is to know, at the flowing of blood, and to the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the rod is corrupted and withdrawn, then you should push or lead the rod with a hollow cane, and urinate for the patient within;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is attached to the head of the rod which has affected those who have not been circumcised, or it has happened due to a wound or an abscess, then you should scrub it with a sharp instrument, so that the threads are disentangled, and the head of the rod is freed from all parts;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a grievous thing to devise this, then you should scrub it with a spatula at no point near the head of the rod and the skin;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then separate it thoroughly between the two, and put the subtle layer of the millstone in a cold frog, so that it does not become stiff again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Surgery is not one of the continuous remedies like the other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Always when we make this work of our will, and properly with children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not practice circumcision on their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of my masters and healers who performed circumcision on the thigh, and with force, and at all novelty;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if it happens that the courses are there because they have two tolls, and by chance if one covers the upper part and delays the lower.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Now it receives a covering, and the pain is double, and at the purification which is given from there, it is not assured of the point of the limb;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and for the purification of the nail by chance scratching the iron, and correcting the joint, and often they are born thus that they have no need of purification and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mending which is done with force all along the thread of the vein I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut evenly on the whole sole beneath;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but let the thread be well stretched around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not make him do more than to tie the thread around the rod as gently, and then you make it slide in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then you make it stand upright between your hands straight, and hold the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so that the veins do not see them, nor any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then put your hand on the rod and blow or heat, and pull it up as high as the head of the rod is in;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then thoroughly clean the area of the wound which has been assembled, then tie it with a double thread, then tie underneath and attach to another thread.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it with the second thread at the pouch and at the index finger, and wrap between the two threads, then lift the cord above hastily and pull the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the remedy;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and on the powder I drizzle glue made from a cooked egg yolk mixed with rose water, congealed with rose oil that is good and fresh, and let it sit until the next day, and treat with another treatment until he is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The shape of the bandages for the wound is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two heads should be even and should be equal, and the heads should also be as large as the equally balanced handle:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of the mundification is when the dead heart falls to the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the liquids make an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and equal coating, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, if you have tenaculum, and then the coating.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they surpass three days, and what is beneath the rod is inflamed, let it be until the abscesses are appeased, and the scab falls off lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you cover it as you can move, and guard against the part of the rod, this will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Healing then the wound of sudden blows with powder, which we have said to treat with powders, and if you cover beyond measure, and it goes to the surface, it will not harm at all.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
dou retenement de l’urine	due to retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from obstruction of the stone, or from congealed blood, or from a blow, or from a new wound, or from similar things, which we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine does not flow, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is there or in the neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be bent over their knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and they should place their feet on the back, and stretch out their belly from the upper part above the back, and the patient should strain to alleviate themselves as much as they can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constricted by the pressure of the stone from above, because of which the urine does not flow;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you administer the extraction with all the instruments which are called "syringe", of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and be of subtle silver threads lightly woven, like the feather of a bird;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let it be the length of a palm and a half, and subtly at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of releasing the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the head with a point of wool or cotton, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and remove the superfluous length of the wool and cut it just to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and the rod with moist olive oil and water tided;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the rod, until it reaches the root of the rod, then bend the rod downwards towards the bowel;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then apply the syringe before it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel it reach the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless the conductor or she who was led astray.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread throughout the entire lane little by little, and the urine follows the lane, then it is extracted further, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And restart the syringe until the bladder is empty, and alleviate the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes into the bladder, where putrefaction is assembled, and you see distilling waters and medicines, if you do all the instrument called "clyster", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if there are three punctures:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see.
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And the veins are sought out by which the medicine can be inserted in such a way that it stops the bleeding well, if one can then draw out the moisture, and apply as much as is necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see gathering your medicines in the bladder, put the head of the cauterizer in the moisture, and pull out the pulling which is inside;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you pull out the moisture to the cauterizer, and then strongly pull back the pulling thing inside;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters inside, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and it is the shape of a subtleclyster which one uses to cleanse the bladder:
si est ci:	if it is so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is made of silver or copper, and its head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below that the vein or the sinewy part;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a bladder of a sheep and put the moisture that you see to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts in the form of a twisted double thread, and heat that moisture over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then put the head of the scalpel in the orifice, then hold your hand on the bladder at all the moisture that comes, so that the patient feels that this moisture has already come to the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle with it, and pierce it roundly all around.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put the strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dal, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as if you had done with the bladder, to press with your hand so that the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already said in the division the ways of piercing, and the extraction together with medicines.
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I have said the difference between the piercing in the groin as wounds, and all the signs, and in what piercing one should operate with regard to size.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the rod;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is born in the bladder happens more often to children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it appears there, and touches the patient's rod, and it bites many times, and then becomes rigid;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at much of these jumps the foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is easy the healing of children until they are 4 years old, and it is much grievous in old people, and it is as youthful moisture, to those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and it is the cure easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to calm the patient by whispering, in order to expel all the bad humors that are in his intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders the quest to pierce the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and push and move upwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and jumps out many times from the high place;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then have him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely downward.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then touch the spine and inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall to the toucher of the whole, anoint your right index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is weak, or your left finger, if the patient is young and complete.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and thrust it into its foundation, and touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, anoint it at the neck of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on it with your finger, and thrust it to the depth where you saw fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch out his right hand above the loins, and with his left hand remove the skin which is beneath the loins in the part where the cut is made.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then he applies the spatula-like instrument, because this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And makes an incision between what is between the hip and the perineum, not in the middle but at the side of the left nostril;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight on the stone, and the two should be thus or in the perineum, and the cutting should be so that it is wide by default, and within it is narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	perhaps the pressure if the two that are in the perineum, so that they jump out of their sense of labor;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is some stone where it has angles, and margins:
si est griés a issir;	if it is difficult to remove;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is some that is underneath, resembling a pebble, and round, whose removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Where there are corners and edges, make the cut larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and it does not jump, so it is necessary that you stretch over the tendons which are like a file on the head, to stretch the stone so it doesn't escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	where you apply underneath the subtle, curved instrument at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot engineer it thus, then enlarge the little hole, and if the sense is deceived, then stretch with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stone, then apply the largest first to the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull out fiercely, and the small ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it requires more careful treatment, and causes greater harm.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For these things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	where he dies, or the urine comes immediately because the bladder cannot hold it;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but you must force yourself to handle it, or to remove the tendons, as far as you can treat them piece by piece;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply the plaster of incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it in place, and put over it a dressing moistened with oil and wine, or with oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then resolve the patient back onto their bed, and do not dislodge the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, rub in the oil and water very well, then apply the ointment of diyafinicon and ointment of basilicon, until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses come in the wound and corrode, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this means that the urine cannot pass, which is known in such a manner without passing with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	put your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrode the bladder, and putrefy it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound of water and of oil and of serum, and aid him in all the ways that you know, so that he may be healthy.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the wounds that you treat, that you bind the two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is conducted by the rod, and fixed in, and the urine cannot issue;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the treatment of those things that I speak of thus, that you cut many times, is an excuse for the cutting through this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a rod of iron in this form and it will be at three angled points fixed in the thigh.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take the thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then push the iron into the rod gently, until it reaches the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the iron with your hand on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If the urine comes too soon, then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone that is within the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it breaks suddenly, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this because of anything that bothers him, then thread the filament beneath the stone and another above, then make the penis in the place of the stone between the two ligaments, then extract it outward, and release the ligament, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until he is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It rarely happens that a stone forms in women, and if it does happen, the treatment is grievous, and is hindered by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-acquainted with her own body, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth manner is that the stones of the woman are deeper than those of the man, because it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear in this. And if you need to ascend to this, it is necessary that you take a wise midwife, and hold the true faith on, and if you do not find one, then ask for a subtle cast;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And it presents a wise midwife in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and she is commanded to do what you command her regarding the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very well if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to thrust her finger or foundation and search for the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and it heals, if the swelling goes down under his hand, and he recommends that he puts his hand or with the patient, and wants and presses his left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	It heals, if it is necessary to move it gently from the entrance of the bladder downwards, until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then feel on the stone at the root of the thigh against the soft flesh, where it is badly arranged, and feel the stone in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his finger on the stone or below, and let the cutting be at the first small size;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the instrument in the incision, if you feel the stone and it grows into the wound so that the stone can come out further, and know that there are many kinds of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to know, small and large and bitter and sweet, long and round, and which have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the symptoms to recognize the disorder.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the saneness fails, then put on the glass vitriol ointment, and hold it in place for an hour until the saneness is established;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is broken, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone as men who will help you in your operation;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the saneness fails, and it is of the artery that is cut, then put the powder on the wound and hold tight with tents and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone alone and do not touch it, lest by chance the patient may die;
puis cure la plaie.	then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the limbs are at rest, so return to your work, until the stone is firm.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramice aquose is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white pus, which is beneath the skin of the thighs, that contains the egg;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly on the web of the uvea, if one believes that it is another eye;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it's the skin of the conjunctiva between the white syfac that we have mentioned;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and they did not have a small pouch.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this remedy is from a weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from a blow on the conjunctiva, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	where it's a declining yellow color, or it's without red, or black, or watery pale, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, because if it's white syfac that we have mentioned, then it's the red abscesses, a little long as the figure of an eye, and doesn't open the conjunctiva, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in its own web, then it's the red abscesses with part of the uvea, and therefore one thinks that it's another eye;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the groin and the white siphac, it feels all right;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you want to know the color of the moisture, it is experienced by the entire introjective quarter, because its form is thus presented.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge from what comes after the internal quarter, of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure by iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to their power and the replenishment of their body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then he puts it on his back, on a thing a little high, and places under him many folds;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then he sits on his left, and instructs the minister to sit on the right, and extends the rod to one of the two ribs of the heart near the groin;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula-like instrument, and cut the skin of the groin between the loin down to the little finger, and make your incision quite straight in dividing the skin of the groin up to the white siphac, and carefully scrape according to their power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the swollen area with a needle full of water, and extract all the water, then put on your onion-like poultices, and the swollen area will subside afterwards.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the core of the wounds, but let the swelling soothe itself;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	take all or piece by piece the subtle tissue of it gently, so that if you do not take it well carefully, the swelling will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the swelling has gone for a time, then reset it in its place when you have accomplished the work of the swollen area;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then assemble the two lips of the wound at a seam, then heal it as with other wounds, until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the swelling corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to lift the veins that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cauterize the entire circumference, and extract the humor, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if it is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	cauterize the other part just as you did the first one equally, then suck out the blood, and put into the wound a lint soaked in rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another lint soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two circumferences, and put double wrapping cloths on top, and bind it all together with a ligature that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with lint dressing according to this similarity and are assembled by stitching into the girdle of the arms, and one of the hands takes hold at the bottom just up to the back, and the other at the part of the thigh;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two heads on the two angles, and so the entire assembly is restrained in the loop of the arm.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and no time is medicine better than the fire cautery at the height of iron, and it is that you take the subtle cautery scalpel, and scrape the skin of the joints, and be careful as we have said, so that the white sap which contains the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery in this form, and pierce that sap as with onions, and scrape it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And you scrape in all the ways that you can, until you uncover everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and beware that the cautery iron does not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more salvageable;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and beware of the deterioration of blood, and dread the operations of iron;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing does contrary, or abscess bursts or blood flows out or something else, if you heal what makes it contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to undergo this treatment because of its horror, then make a small perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain through the signs we have said that the watery fluid is there, then seat the patient on a high-backed chair;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then prick the abscess at the lowest part beneath all the spatula-like tissue, and put the perforation two finger-lengths from the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the pores be wide, so that all the watery fluid flows out freely;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let the remaining watery fluid flow out, then heal it until the wound is healthy;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and he should not let the white cloth issue forth from the mouth of the wound, if it is necessary that you apply a pen or instrument by which one draws out the water of the hydrops, whose form is thus before;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarges the wound, and knows that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or soon afterwards, and when it is assembled thus before, and then the patient will spend his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Knows that in the treatment of this arm there is fear in more than one disposition, because it seems to me that many are worth more than leaving it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come to a head, and likewise are burned.
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive anger and anguish, which is expanded as wounds, or of percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not find a point of pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance it is a grievous abscess, painful and piercing, and of a dark color, and often comes from inflammation of an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from inflammation of an artery, it is known by the disposition of hot abscess, when you press on it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not matter if you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from swelling of a vein is known by its disposition to the expression of touching with the fingers, and one can well make the measurement according to this resemblance, and on other symptoms;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you take the care of the wounds, then establish the egg white above, and remove the excess of the white skin, and deliver the suspensor from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already mixed with these new flesh, then it is necessary that you treat the egg, and take care of it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is on the skin, or in that which is inside the veins, then it is necessary that you deliver all this tension, and take care of it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is where the skin is behind, it is necessary that you cut all of it, and extract the humor, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are accomplished, apply the poultice of mild lime oil and rose oil, then treat with other treatments until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	These are abscesses wrapped in a wrapping similar to a poultice, with the softening of the wounds, and the patient's grievance increases greatly when it is seen;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this disease is very close to the fearful one that was before, and in every way we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then place the suspension of the joints below his two buttocks, near all the vessels that are close to the penis, and you tie the masters, and stretch them out forcibly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut to the spatula, trenchant large and traverse the area of the vessels, until they are discovered, and then strip away from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then fix a needle or where it has a double thread, and tie it to the first joint or where the vein was visible, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them in a straight line, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt humors.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heal the wound as with others or by enlarging the opening, so that no vessel bleeds that nourishes one of the joints.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because for this reason there is no point of evil, and if all the veins are visible, it is necessary to treat the joints on all the veins;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their adjustment by the incision of the veins, and they should be steady and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of the Syphac
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The circumstances of this fracture are by the section that comes from the Syfac, or the extension onto the belly in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that route to one of the joints;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this route is either from the Syfac, or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from percussion, or from a fall, or from a blow, or from the lifting of a heavy load, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the Syfac, are that it happens little by little, in a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and it is the abscesses equal as far as the ulcer, because the swelling presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the swelling of the intestine, which brings sudden severe pain at its beginning, and they are diverse abscesses appearing beneath the skin, close by, and it is because of the issue of the intestine and the body's decay due to the swelling.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it descends beneath the ribs with the intestine, and is held back, and causes great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron with fear, because he thinks of escaping from it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to hold their intestine in their hand inside the wound, if they can re-enter it;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then let it be sewn up on its neck between your hands, and lift the thighs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then place the heart above, and cut all the skin of the joints down to the long part;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then thrust inside the leaves of the waist uncinated according to what you have need to open the wound, and be such that the eyes can issue forth;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrub off the swelling that is beneath the skin of the joints, so that the hard white swelling may be uncovered on all parts;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your finger index in that which follows the joint, in that which is between the white swelling that is beneath the skin of the vein, and between the second swelling, and separate that which is behind the vein, and between the second swelling;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then put the right hand inside the curve of the loins, and extend the white cloth upwards to the left hand, and lift the vein towards the entire waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to extend the vein upwards, and detach what is behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and examine your fingers if there is a point of intestine wrapped around or hard white cloth, and if you find nothing, then thrust it into the belly below;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle with a large thread made of X threads, and thrust it into the rear part of the vein, which is behind the skin of the loins;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	behind the waist, then cut the heads that appear as threads, until there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and bind the vein, which we have said is behind the skin of the loins, with a strong ligature of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then wrap the heads of the veins, and bind them in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them cannot enter within, so that abscesses do not grow there.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put a ligature according to the first ligature a long way from that one, and after these two ligatures leave enough space which is beneath the heart of the conjoined fingers, the width of a finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and afterwards all the others according to the roundness that the egg carries.
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut into the part that is beneath the skin of the fingers, until the blood flows, and the swelling, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then mix the millet flour in oil, and put it on the wounds, and I will mix the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And no time is it cauterized with a thread as we have said, after the incision, by fear of deterioration of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature until it sticks by itself.
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it delays at the wound, let it be raised with warm water, and put on what we have said, until it heals;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then heal the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is done as the antimony which is assembled at the seam of the vein, in such a manner that you bind the vessels, after cutting lightly underneath;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut into the middle, and treat the abscess of what is swollen, until the vessels heal;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and opens the muscles;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not descend to any of the intestines as coils, and if they descend, it is little, and repair all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and whenever it stays too long at this point, if he believes the wound or syphilis, so much that the intestines descend;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the swollen face which is like a nut, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and inflates the eyes and opens;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the treatment is by cauterization, as we have said before;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is never cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and it is that the patient places himself on his back between your hands, then holds the arm of the affected limb inflated according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the swelling that is beneath the skin where it hurts, then take the rod and place it on the arm appearing swollen;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press at the deepest part of the belly, then cut the two appearing eyes of the swelling on the head of the rod, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then extract the head of the vein, and do not touch the spot where the blood does not spread to another area, just as I have made you aware in the treatment of intestinal ulcers.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then heal by healing the wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if it is mended and the wound is cured, so that it may be healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The face is constricted, and has no appearance in the rut, and the cauteries are moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the thighs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times are softened the skin of the joints in some men, because the flesh that is within them is softened, and it is easy to see.
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure, that one makes the patient sit up straight, and covers the skin that is softened on the natural skin.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring the two lips together to a seam, and if you see, first remove the excess of the softened skin at three seams or four firmly.
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cover between the seams, and heal it as with other wounds, until it be sound, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	of punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that cauterizations are recommended in our law, and therefore I would prefer not to speak of them in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary to discuss them for they can be done in two ways:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	where one is that the masters respond in writing when one demands it, and in writing the treatment;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have need of cauterization of certain beasts to help us, such as goat and sheep and deer and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say then that cauterizations are done according to two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by attraction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water, until its hide is softened and relaxed;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them with your hand, until they are restored and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the treatment of wounds:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the best, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then lift the suspensor, and sew on each bone to the cop, when you have well excavated them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and let none of the thick skin and the subtle skin that is above the veins;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of treatment is better than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction something of the joints often remains, for which reason the best desires luxury;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then heal the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	and the hemorrhoids
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphrodite is according to two manners of men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two joints appears as if the figure of a woman's nature, where there are hairs, and sometimes it cuts off the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, and it has on the little finger as a rod and they bind.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of the wound and the fame is that you should clean all the adjacent areas, and treat them as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second manner, of men whose urine passes through the skin of their thighs, if there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tendonitis
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tentigen is an adjacent area on the natural part, so much that it is too shameful to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tentigen from your hand or from the onions, and clean it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not rub too much in depth, lest corrupted blood comes, then the treatment of another wound as long as it is healthy;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and to another sore that grows at the mouth of the marrow, and the putrid matter, and by chance it bursts forth, and it is according to the resemblance of a cowe, and for this reason the old people called it "cowe disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you take it, as we have said about the tenderness, and the treatment until it is healthy.
de erratique	of burnings
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Error occurs when the nature of the woman is not well perceived, or the pertussis is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is natural from birth, or it happens by accident due to a disease that came about;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is by chance encounter, or subtle douleur or thick, and it is made deep in the marrow, or in the ribs, or beneath, or whatever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and they hinder conception, and childhood, and by chance they have flowers to have;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this is through the observation of the patient's pulse.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppings are nearly apparent, then seek at your fingers or in the vein.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a subtle douleur and it is close to the liver, if you hurry, and the roundness then:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	place your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then the two livers are formed, so that the subtle douleur is round, and it is above the swellings;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take the thread, and the vein in oil, and place it on the limb, and instruct the woman to stay at home each day, so that she cannot strain.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the skin is hard and thick, it is necessary to take the cupping glasses similar to a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the swelling is from newborn flesh, then suspend it from the hook and the scalpel;
