et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and there are stain-releasing medicines of blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and ensemble of abundant egg whites;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a bandage of wide plaster, so that the wound cannot strain;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and let it be for a long time, and apply a dressing of dry linen;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be cured by other treatments until he is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when new flesh comes in the marrow, it is necessary to apply a cup according to this method, if there are no swollen abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is swollen in the marrow, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Embrocations are openings of veins where there is no crust forming, and when the embrocations are old, they become thin.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similarities of those, and the signs, and I will tell you here those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thigh, when they are deep in the marrow, and they do not appear to sensation, if it is not the cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the marrow, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, afterwards stretch out the tendons as tentacles, and cover with its roots, then powder with medicines restricting blood flow, such as aloe and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then soak her feet in cold water for an hour, then put her in cold air;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if blood comes out, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and peel of green apples and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stagnates, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, have her wear loose garments on her back and arms without constriction;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take a linen cloth, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of angelica with old wine, and make it adhere to the limb.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess breaks, then clean the limb of putrid matter until it is healthy;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough scalp, so it must be covered as I have said in the thesis;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then clean it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the chest
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come to the marrow, such as cancer and pierous abscess and herpes and estoimenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary therefore that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that collect pus;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look if the abscesses are agitated at the beginning of their coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make me ure so long as the pain is appeased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have small stools or he leans against them, and supports himself on his back and brings his feet together in parts to reduce the swelling of the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his knees be expanded, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a band of linen;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck the swelling towards the right side, and I will show you the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the marrow, from which afterwards comes the form;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you have seen how to handle this instrument, you fix the rod first in order to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not go further in than it should, and it does not harm the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the swelling is larger, it is necessary to cover the deepness of the marrow of the torn tendons, so that the swelling does not bother them;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary to put the point of the instrument above, and to hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses open, and one feels it with the hand, if it is necessary to cover at the head, with a spatula, lightly.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the wound is empty, it is necessary that you put into the wound tender moistures in rose oil, or in dry green oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the tender force of the wound at the depth of the marrow, and put below the marrow and on the wounded vein a nettle moisture in water or evil beak thus they are cured.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal afterwards for two days of anointing, coming to this, so that it may be healthy.
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and at no time lift the marrow and the wound by injection of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and a long aristology should be applied;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then reapply to the joint.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set in the marrow, it is necessary to beware of cauterizing with iron, but rather heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of the swelling
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is better first to consider the natural formation of the child and the signs are when you see the woman approaching below, and desire to smell the air:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then hasten the children to issue forth;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then know that this child's birth is according to natural formation, and it is the issue under its head, and the second one with him;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, you must gently press his belly, so that the child issues forth quickly;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends upon its head, the second one is with him, and the marrow of his superfluous parts is purified by good mundification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes against the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or above, and is converted by an accident on its neck, and by other bad postures;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	it is necessary at the handling that it be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the infant comes upon its head by natural means, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the strength of the one is feeble, then make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and raise its natural oil or fenugreek being cooked, and then put the handling between its two little spatula-like tools which are its form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and anoint the second one, and apply to his finger as much as the moisture that is there corrects the fires;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and bind the belly of the woman so that the children descend, and if they do not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with a mixture of fenugrec with oil of sesamum;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her take and absorb a concoction, and hold her mouth and nostrils for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	if the children are now strangled.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands issue forth fire, it is necessary that you reset them lightly little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then rock the seat on the ground, and hold onto the woman, so that she does not fall at the rocking;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if he cannot put his hand in, and the infant dies, if he catches the hands at the counter which is placed beforehand, and extracts the child, and resets equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes onto its feet, if it is necessary to cast upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps just to the knees, if he commands to grasp, and makes it straighten with condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps far, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump far as we have said, turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come far as we have said, take a mixture of high water, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and crush all in the mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put it on the nature of the woman inside and drive out this anointing, then make her sit in warm water until beneath the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened below, have him make a collar of myrrh, and put it below, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have him sit on the chair, then have him straighten up and hold his mouth and nose, and take a light hold of his belly, for he will now faint.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child onto its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the faintness comes in this form, then you put your hands on his belly little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then he should be supported on his neck, and his feet should hang down, and he should be laid out on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold his hands little by little, and then take hold of his hands on the belly, and remove the cushions from below, until he is laid out downwards;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the faintness does not leave him, take his feet and move them gently, then move his belly upwards, then he will recover from your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and warm the little child gradually;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to take hold of it as much as the infant sucks.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child who comes out with a wide hand meanwhile
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	You must skillfully bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if you cannot bring it back, lift the woman up and go.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, make her sit on the bed, and bend her legs forcefully;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then treat the muscle strain that I have mentioned;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she is not inflamed, make her sit on a chair, then study how to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and warm the infant according to its natural shape, and make it straighten out, and instruct it to take hold as much as the infant sucks strongly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the release of the child on its neck, and it has expanded its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	You must skillfully guide its hand, then turn it little by little, and warm it lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then place on its natural muscle tone of the high and oil, as we have said, then instruct it to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, then make him sit on the seat, and instruct him to take hold;
et la fai esternuer.	and make him stretch out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the secondary ones
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it returns to this manner entirely the second time, then touch the second [joint] with your finger, as long as the moisture is evacuated;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if it falls upon his face and neck, then touch the swelling, so that it is not retained, and soothe the boy;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as long as you have placed him as it should be, and instruct the woman to take hold at no time;
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will be easier afterwards.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that a gem grows many times, and sometimes three or four grow at once.
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and it is not a strange thing, and it happens little.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live, if little known;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they should be multiplied, and are separated by the syphac who divides them, which is tied to the bud;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they issue naturally like all those under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they issue grievously, thus the cure as we have said, and let the subtle balm be, and make it thick and light, what it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is worth more to health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious wisdom, and it is necessary that the balm knows all this, for by chance similar things have happened.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	do thus according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman with a dead fetus or in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained by manual operation;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has not had an accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her thighs be inclined downwards, and her legs be raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife holds the two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not torn apart by the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then anoint the mouth of the womb with oily moistures made from walnut and fenugreek and flaxseed, then oil the bath with these oils and these anointments;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	Then put the buttons in the marrow lightly, then seek the place where they put the onions that are suitable for this, and take care that the veins appear to be prepared to descend to their head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if you place the onions in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descents are on foot, hold them or prick them and the sides of the month;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that you hold the onion in your right hand, and put the curve between the fingers of your left hand, and lightly touch all of your hand, and place the onion in none of these places that we have said, until it comes to the evacuated thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and that is the shape of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then place against another onion, or the third where you have mastery, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then it is set evenly by moving from one side to the other, so that it comes out straight, and let the edges of the teeth be for holding, as this is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if it remains in one part, oil the bail with some of its fingers, and put them in that part, and treat the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if it does not remain at all, put this edge or higher up, and do this until it issues forth completely free.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back due to stiffness, then you must wrap around the drapil, until it issues forth completely.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then cup the joint of the sole or at the heel, and thus you must do with the other hand, and with the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the infant is large and it is constricted at birth, or it has an assembled stiff neck, then you must put the spinous spatula between your two, and make the head and extract the stiffness.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	where you apply the instrument called "almidach", which is one of the instruments or surgical tools that come after this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus it makes the veins naturally have a great natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then treat the bones like tenons, and the head jumps forward and holds onto the strength, if it is fractured, as long as the moisture that is or worse comes out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces in the muscle where you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on its feet, then it is light attraction, and the remedies at the mouth of the marrow are lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is strained in the belly or in the thigh, then it is necessary that you extract it with the drapil enveloped around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make an incision in the belly or thigh, until the moisture that is there flows;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are numb, and the head remains still, then he puts his hand in front of the marrow, and draws it just up to the mouth of the marrow;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then he applies the ninth or tenth, and draws it strongly;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed by hot abscess that has come, then it does not need to be worked, but rather to be treated with moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the treatment is with plasters, and they should be in watery, softening, and moisturizing (applications).
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it upright, then treat it with what we have said regarding the living infant;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and so that one cannot obtain power, if one draws strongly by sections, and does not leave anything of the secondary (affected area).
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, remind him of what we have said about abscesses that come in the marrow;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if blood flows out, let it be put into warm water, and remind him of other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb an infant had been dead, then she conceived another on top of that one, and rejected the dead one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long tension the wind came into the belly, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to great portent.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long tension, and could not soothe the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong plaster of attraction, and an bone came out, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because it seemed that the belly had no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I touched the wound, and I treated it with my hands, until the woman was at her best point;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I watched over the woman for a long time afterwards, and then I gave her a little drink of good wine.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I did not forget this chapter because of that which, when the masters find a strange thing, they know how to put it right.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, where one examines the books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and it has two turnings as it has two heads of the veins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle on the restrainer, and made of ebony or boxwood.
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the tube be wide, and the margin of the trees should be, and from a palm and a half;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the middle of the two limbs should be the adjustments of this same tube, which are fastened at one end and the other, half a palm in length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and this adjustment is placed in the mouth of the clamp to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, in its more subtle and lighter likeness, should be made from ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of the pincers.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and have two heads with two adjustments, as you see, a palm in length, and two widths;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you want to open the clamp with all the instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet pendant and her legs covered, then place the two adjustments assembled in the clamp, and hold the head of the instrument down between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then open your hand to the entire instrument, as you have done with the even tendons, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the marrow, until the boil does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all elevated, and their similarities are multiplied there;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the mirrors have appeared to them, so much more swift is the work, and higher are the bones among them according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in infancy, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his wing, and then make him stretch out his condition, and hold your hands on the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and let him jump through that, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take the poultice, and make a perforation or covering, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calmant, rue, anise, chamomile, sassafras, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or put in water on the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a cane or tube into the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the patient, and hold it as long as the vapors come out from the patient;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make them sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondary symptom appears quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not get better, instruct the patient to anoint their left hand with oil of sesame or musk, and then put it in the nostril, and desire the second one;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when they have found it, take hold of it and stretch it little by little, straightening it so that the patient does not feel extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but you must move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then draw it out;
si venra et se desaerdra.	If he comes and dislocates himself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the thigh is already constricted, we have described the treatment of sternutation, and of fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all that we have said, beware that you do not fall into error in treating;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the thigh, you apply it to the hip of the woman, then anoint it with a four-drug ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if it will putrefy and suppurate, and come to a crisis;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nevertheless, when it putrefies thus, there comes bad smell from the stomach and head, and blinds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	It is necessary therefore to use soothing fumigations for that:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	none of the ancients have experienced fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one fumigates the woman at the retention of the flowers and of the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to make similar to a dog, and place the subtle head in nature, and the large heads above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the tar until it is roasted, and recommence another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation perceived, thus the aid has been subtly stopped:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	it is necessary then to give to the patient who perceives it thus with his finger, and does not touch the spatula with the ague, and arrange the bandage so that it does not touch;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the affected limb a mixture of wine and oil, then the treatment of anointing until it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not rest, then put or insert a piece of lead, and leave it there for days, and be careful when the infants want to go to their chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And often these stoppings come suddenly from a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	it is necessary to cover that sudden one:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if it be cured, as we have said about the falling of the spleen.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula at the bottom
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from beneath the foundation are nodes, and those that come from beneath the deep foundation are furrows, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that node is ancient, it opens, and gathers moisture in a whitish or subtle swelling, and at no time are these fistulas persistent;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by the fact that there is a flow or flatulence when the patient makes an effort to eject, and sometimes suddenly jumps upwards.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the rod;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and they reach just to the joint of the thigh, and just to the top of the hip.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the persistent fistula by its foundation, and it does not hide.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you apply your indexed finger to the foundation, and insert a subtle needle of iron or copper into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, you insert a subtle probe of lead, or a horse hair, until you feel the probe or the hair with your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from bad pertussis or evacuation or twisting or vermin, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not pierce badly;
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is close to the bladder or near the urinary tract, if it affects the urine, and cannot be soothed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just up to the joint of the thigh, then the probe comes just to the place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the origin of the pain is within, then it is that it is immediately swollen, and no medicine or sudden movement by anointing is of value;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure unless one works hard, and vanity of foolish doctors who get involved.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In one that is not persistent and not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient places himself between your hands on his back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts his legs up to his knees, and has his knees bent towards his stomach;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then apply a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it in the foundation, then it is necessary that you apply your right index finger, and afterwards it seems that the tent has penetrated;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and be discovered where you feel between your fingers the swelling or the flesh, then know that it is persistent;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work carefully, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can hardly ever fully heal some wounds, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that one does, if it is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and the entire hot iron is in the fistula, until it reaches the bottom;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these burned scars are dry, which resemble a bird's claw;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat the moist wounds with powder, until those scars are dry, then treat them with ointment, soothing and drying.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, no other way can it be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and it holds within, and does not penetrate just to the finger that is at the bottom, and between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula at what follows the covering of the hollow gut;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If you cauterize at the beginning of the fistula, and cut beforehand beneath the tent, and then apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be freed, and will fall;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then I will define those withered branches that seem a bird's wing, and none of them will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you feel faint, and shorten between you and the vein, then cautery with fire or medicine is necessary.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cauteries assemble two bone things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	it is to know, the dryness of those withered branches, and the staunching of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the treatment of wet tents in mud or in broken wood, until the juices flow out, and it makes the withered branches dry in the mud;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of the swollen fingers by applying dry charcoal, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes almost to the font of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then cut off your finger or foundation, and inquire about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between there is the cloth or the suture or flesh, or it is near to piercing, if there are no other ways than the way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	where you cauterize as we have said, or you sew just to the foundations, or if you can put tente and cure as at first;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in the foundation, so you do not sew the holding that holds the foundation, and come to the gestures through the voluntary sense;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then the cure, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance it will be healthy, or you remove that covering and the world then it is sewn from the deep foundation, or by tente or by another appointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then define that faulty flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	Then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the weakened part at the foundation:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And often are fistulas in this manner:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is or costs the depth of the foundation beneath the skin above, if you take a perforated tent at the head in this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you push the twisted thread into it, and push the tent onto all the threads in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	It is piercing into the margin of the foundation within, then pull out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you push with your finger or foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and hold one to the other, and let it be for a day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it often, until the thread grips these flesh that are between two, and cicatrizes;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound so it is sewn up and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all ways that you can, unless it is too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make a copper plate for the dressing wound if it is deep inside, and then the cure, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine of the backbone where the fistula is made is very narrow and piercing;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not, because one cannot cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of bruises
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Wounds are classified in two manners:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	where they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they cut short the blood flow, and there is one or more, and they destroy the foundation and at the head of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are deep have little moisture, and they cut short or a little of citrine water or a little of blood, and they have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those that have them deep in the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to stretch out to go into chambers, until the foundations issue forth, and they appear as threads;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hasten, and he bends as tendons, or you hold it at your finger, then he covers in his roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tendons cannot hold them back due to their moisture, if they take it to the apron, or to the cushion, or a piece of chamelot;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and stretch them with your fingers, then cover, and sprinkle above some hot powders that are in the fire of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize as it is said or according to the chapter of cautery, then heal with other cures until he is healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundament cannot issue, then clisterize the patient with a biting and harsh clyster to cleanse that which is in the fundament, so that it can issue openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	as the patients cannot hold themselves, and if their vein is outside the fundament, then the treatment is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them in your finger or nails, and grasp them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	It is fitting that you adjust the bandage in this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take the thread, and put it on a needle, and then pull the thread above and make a piercer with the needle from another part, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and if it is double;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the dressing a clean cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he should rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it cool down as much as it congeals, and when they are cooled, if they receive treatment of ointment and other treatments, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	to dry the wounds or dressing
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often it happens that there is a burning of fevers in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you remove the point of a splint or of your nail the crust above, which does not let it get moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat until it is sooted as it is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be sooted, then recommence the rubbing more strongly than before, until it is very healthy, and is scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat until it is healthy.
dou fremit	two fremits
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formice is a small faulty appearance against the body, and goes very deep in.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the coldness, and one feels it as if dead from shivering, and it comes into all the body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread from a bird's feather, or a strong thread of wild duck, and put that thread on the fracture, so that the circles penetrate the fracture entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around the entire thread so that you grasp everything entirely around the fracture, and put it in the front, and draw out the fracture from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a frame of a cord or iron in this form, and be subtle underneath and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	do not pierce, because you must hold at the finger, and press strongly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, if you cauterize the fracture, as if it is before or in a chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Never make an injection of silver or copper, or of melted lead or vermillion;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and never use those small and large instruments, according to the ones to which they are accustomed.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore which one prepares in the treatment of children who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cluster, small and large, is above large, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and it has a displacement where the stomach is tied, as you see, and the chest is perceived inside.
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and it has on one of the sides two perforations, and in the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and it has the stomach where one puts medicines in a bladder of beast or parchment, and is perceived all around with many small perforations, and has between each perforation one inch of space, then put in these perforations a strong thread twisted into an X or circle, and assemble the stomach as if it were a bag.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, then tie it to the instrument in front of with a strong thread, then cleanse.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and that's the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clister with oil or album of egg, or similar thing, then put it in lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then the minister's hands are applied to his II (two) hands together, so that they may be entirely visible, then extract the cluster, and raise the patient's legs to the partition, and if the medicine wants to issue, if it can hold as much as possible.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a night entirely, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat the illness of decay of the stomach, and the medicine hastens to exit, then recommend it as much as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the ulcers are in the foundation, or abscess, then the cluster should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the shape of the subtle cluster above where the skin can be held in place:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds.
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by thrust of stone, and cut of sword and of knife, or of lance or of stick or of arrow, or of similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where wounds are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the feet, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come into its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, beware if it is a matter of stones or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is great, and you doubt lightly of a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it makes the cephalic wound somewhat healthier, meanwhile if little blood comes from the wound, and let the healing be contrary to the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient's fullness of wine and coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, let his meat be diminished, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if abscesses and ulcers come, a cotton moistened with rose oil or wine steeped in it;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, so it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will mention a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has moved it, put on some ointments, until it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword's cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by tending, if they are assembled by stitching, as I will say about wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and bursts, and no longer holds but a little, then cover it.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then heal the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as tested and roasted meat, also like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a skin with putridity, and it does not adhere to the bone, so cut around the putridity entirely, and throw far away, then cure.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has entered into the wound or vein, without delay, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, so seek to cut the artery, and if you find it dislocated, so tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not benefit, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you apply this powder which absorbs in this way so that the arsenic does not move.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	Take incense, a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Dragon's blood, two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	living chalk, three parts, and powder subtly, and fill the wound, and hold firmly, until it adheres well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind well, and let it not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not stop the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time does one make a poultice of living chalk solely, when one has not incense nor dragon's blood, but rather the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arrow has moved in the wound, meanwhile in this state, if you do not put a little of this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it begins to suppurate;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment, and not to put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation from there is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be soothing, if you heat it in warm water, and mix it with rose oil, and cook it also in warm water, and other mined remedies according to this method, and apply moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up with thread, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, then prick or pierce at a lower level;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize, for that is the craft of surgery;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular, and the conduits are guarded, because the flesh goes, then sew the jugular onto the canal of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it firmly, and let no days pass, then heal the wounds of the joints so that they are healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it out;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, seek them out thoroughly, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound festers, and separate and align the outlet;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then make the treatment thus as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from a wound of a spear or dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it's a cut from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if the wound has become putrid where the patient's ailment comes from:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, put the powder on it at the first hour, do not bind it with a bandage that would hinder it from scarring deeply, and let it heal by itself, and cure the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I apply attractive ointment, and the patient recovers twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, put a lot of cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there comes no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, it is not restrained by the veins of the arm;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the thumb of tendons and other treatments, until it be sound;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and close up, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is as one ought.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or in the chest or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, of stitching;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has caught pieces, so that it wounds, and the torn fibers if they are dislocated;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not dislocated, let the wound purify, then ease the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds to other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	because of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The remedies for the belly are large, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the large wound sometimes the intestine, or the knots of the intestines, because of the introjection of them;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more painful, and sometimes it is better to have a small wound than a large one, because one puts the intestines back in place more easily, if one does not put them back hastily;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Because the intestine swells so much that it feels cold, if it returns to points, and because it makes the inner wound worse, because one must reset the intestine to its place like others do.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common stitches have in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body and the two other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and however they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will tell each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is outside, and a gentle thing is to put back, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is frosty, heat it up partially in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Soak a sponge or a cloth in warm water suddenly, or you cook in warm water and squeeze and press, and stir the intestine until the inflammation is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and many times make these wines restraining, and it is worse than the sole for dis-inflaming.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the inflammation departing, if you moisten the intestine with warm water or hot wine and evil humors are cooked, for by this the entry is alleviated a little;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound with an instrument by which one collects the humors;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is worse than the surgery, that we should not perform it without great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and it's the instruments for the wound:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut within the curve and do not dig too deep, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.
