je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and freed it, and pulled it out strongly, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose arrow has fallen in his back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and left the arrow within him, and did not change its natural disposition, nor did I find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, whose arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he remained thus, suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And pulled out an arrow from the king's prince's man, which was stuck in his knee, and it was slightly leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and it was the arrow totally removed.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to the treatment after she had fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought a subtle pulse in her entire body, and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt numbness and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow; I put on the affected place a digestive attractive plaster, because the abscesses did not inflame.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the abscess of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put on the plaster for many days, and healed the wound again, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day within his nose.
et il le me dist.	and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on the wound a corrosive medicine for many days, until it was opened, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which adhered to the flesh.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I applied to the opening of the wound by that medicated ointment, so much that the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it progressed well within four months, and then I relaxed if the wound was closed where I applied the tourniquets, and the swelling on one side and the other, and could not exit;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to subtily and ingeniously make devices, until I took it in hand with well-made tourniquets, according to what its form would be at the end of this chapter, so that I treated it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror shows that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, for the book cannot take everything in.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare well a little great thing, and on what is present and failing, they find new work, and new instrument, in the understanding of the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that the arrows do not issue from the limbs where they are fixed, except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps forth by there where it enters, it is the arrow entering into their flesh, and it does not jump forth at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is porous around, and the outlet is cleared;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot exit, let it be thus for some days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, one should prick into the entire forest subtly, so that the eyes within are enlarged, and then the tract.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the chief's head, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not extract it, but let it be until it is even after some days, for if the arrow comes just to the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed in the bone, and does not come out by itself, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then the engine to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very fixed in and cannot be extracted further, one should administer tareres within, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has been repelled into the body of the corpse so that it cannot be seen, one should search everywhere for it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel, if it resists against any instrumental examination;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve, so it makes sense that the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow where it holds, so cut the flesh that is attached to two parts of the muscle where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, until you can extract it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtly take care that you do not break the arrow, so that you extract it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, let it stay until the surrounding tissue is purified, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you oppose, so amend what we have said about the treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of the incision near the nerve and vein, and set in motion how you can extract the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the form it was when the arrow fell in, for it is the greatest aid that it be, and if you cannot, so arrange it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it appears with no sign of it, or the skin is inflamed in that place if one sees or feels by touch:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut then so much, as long as the tongs can grasp, and then extract:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly, so that it enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the remainder of the arrow is there, cut around all the remainder;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the remainder is small, and you want to administer a cutting, if you administer an instrument cut, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And then apply fire, and if the arrow is barbed, he applies the instrument to a precise point entering inside, in order to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the veins are, so you can, then heal the wound as it suits.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow has struck the hand or foot or in the belly or in the bladder or in the ribcage, and it is close by, and you can reach over, he reaches over.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of touching the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if that is your profession.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the button-like head is like the claw of a bird, for pushing at the point of the arrow, as it is the shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs to hollow out and to extract if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are thirty-one veins from which one bleeds, of which sixteen are in the head, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are apparent in the two temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the eyelids of the eyes, which are called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two gullets which are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the head, and simple people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basalic, and simple people call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilisk is on the right side, and they call it the "vein of the belly", and it is on the spleen, and it is the one that is felt, which appears manifestly on the groin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the auricular and the anular, and if it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the hollow of the left side, and the second Sophene which is at the ankle of the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The wisdom of the veins that are behind the ears helps against ancient cataracts and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the healer, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the limb where the veins are like a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then strain the patient's neck to a vision, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in the two vessels depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	where the fingers give you pain, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, it is a sign of anemia;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and insert it beneath the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein above, and cut through the skin and the vein well, two inches deep, and make the blood flow out until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and lift, until it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is to emigrate an ancient vein, and soothing, and accustomed optalmia, and in the course of the bitter tears as the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the health of the veins if it is so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient strains his neck, so much that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse beneath your finger, and then signs of an inflammation;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the heart onto the vein above your finger's tip, and insert the lance beneath, and lift the vein above, and the cupping, just as you have done with the other veins, and make the blood flow according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then lay down the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then apply a formation, and let it be until it is healthy;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their coupling and their extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The health of the vein at the forehead is worth as much as the health of the cephalic area, for old facial diseases, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting, so much that the veins appear;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and lay the vein as it should be healthy and never again will the swelling occur from a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	In no way, it is not suitable for the flames to be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the wound across, because the bone is near, and by chance break the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The wound of the two veins that are in the two arms helps with the eyes, and the tendon, and the reddening, and the orifice in the eye, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their wound is that the patients strain their neck by twisting in no direction, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the wound, and let the wound be across, a little deep, a little long, a little wide of the flame, for there is no spot of flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make a correction of the blood, as much as you have mastery, and then lay it on a cushion, and lay it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The wisdom of the vein that does not know how to cure, and suffers from being overwhelmed, and from facial diseases, such as migraines and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the vein is such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with his left hand, and takes the subtle flame in length, and inserts it into the liver in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well in this way, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep in the fontanel, and make the blood flow according to your need, then leave it for a night, for it is almost completely restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The vein of the two gundeges helps with the constriction of the wingbone, and with the beginning of messelry, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosions, and herpes, and similar things.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the health is such that the patient strains his neck now one way and then another, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master stand above the patient's head, and the patient sits on a stool, then opens the vein of the arm a little widely, then draws out the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary;

et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until morning, so that the wound may be healthy.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins above the liver is affected by gathering at the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and painful nostrils and within.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the health is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the leaf, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right leaf and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Here is the translation:
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health from beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the health of the head, and it's at the constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the veins is such that the patient's blood appears between your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	examine then one and the other, and do not insert too deeply, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck where one usually examines are examined in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where we prick with a flame making a large scar, or subtly with an olive-shaped instrument as if cutting into the neck, and it is called "aneuil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame-like burning is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veined surfaces plainly with a lot of apparently thick blood, and that they contain a lot of blood and turmoil;

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed moderately, and that he beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one should not be pricking the inflammation, but rather cutting in this way skillfully.

ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	where you want no vein of it, or you feel in its place the vein in the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it appears manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the joint at the flame anesthesia, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the vein, it is necessary also that you stretch out the arm, so that you touch the place as much as you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of the incision, and then stretch out the arm, and cut into the vein at the flame anesthesia;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not strike into the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is an artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid that then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flowing upward like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is not from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Here is the translation:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Here is the translation:

Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not cleansed, and it becomes infected, and the medicine does not present itself, then cut the artery so it opens, for the head of the veins returns;
et estainche li sans.	and cleanse the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a dressing of figs, and apply it, and take one of the medications and place it well just up to the other joint;

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The health of the vein in the middle is thus aided so that it draws blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be aware that he warms himself by the nerve which is underneath, and if he presses too much in the wrong place, and he cuts the nerve, and he swells and the healthiest becomes grievously ill, and perhaps cannot heal;

Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the muscles, then they make a scar far from it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The health of the head is assisted, which draws blood from the head, and assists the eyes;

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about healing is that health is not maintained except by preserving healthiness and avoiding future diseases.

Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing that is administered for the diseases has no determined hour, but only when need is of day or of night, in all hours and at all times.

s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant. And if he touches the healthy area, after a large amount of blood has been let out, it is necessary that he should have a broth made from meat, and a subtle and fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the section or chapter on fainting, for evacuating the vein.

Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to bleed twice, then let it bleed in the same spot, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy in the place of the vein at the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts their hand in warm water, until the flesh becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then bleed now from the crossing, not too large nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the large wounds be, and be well close to the joint of the hand, and if you cannot issue from it, reset the hand in warm water, and let the blood flow in the warm water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in winter, do not reset the hand in warm water, for they put it more in ivy than in winter.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the wound of this vein is healthier than all other wounds, for it has neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The wound of the salvation of the right hand is good for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand steady, and put it in warm water, until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the wound is across, and if you cut through everything entirely, do not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not put too much pressure, for the nerves are very sensitive to cold, and then put your hand in warm water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and it cannot issue.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn out the blood as much as is necessary for you, then put oil on the vein and sew it up hastily, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sanity of the left hand is worth more than the disease of the right, and do everything just as I told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wisdom of the sphere is worth all the diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his blood is such that the patient's foot is swollen in warm water, and rubs against the vein until it perishes, and lays above the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they go out in many branches;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	look for the one that is larger or thicker, or at the ankle, which is more useful.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you feel the veins under the foot, beware of the nerves that are very sensitive, and the vein of traversing also as in a cupping.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the sans cannot issue from it, then put the foot in water, and let the vein well empty itself.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the surgeons fail the first time, they start again from above a little, because the joints are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make it equal on the other side in harmony.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The joints of the sciatic vein are at the junction of the thigh, and its wound is worth the pain of the hip, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his wound is such that the patient goes between bad and good, and extracts above the flesh in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then the wound heals in all the ways that you can, and by crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth more that you bind it, for the joints are sound, and it is much restored to many people's hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then no vein of those that open or give two fingers, and towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and do so much correction of the blood that you see, and then loosen the bandage, and put on cotton and hold steady;
ele est maintenant sanee.	he is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	the blood flows from a cupping device
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or of brass, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and attracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping without striking is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with full fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping done by striking and extracting blood is done in 14 places of the body, where one is all in a lump on the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping of the two hips;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping on the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cuppings in the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cuppings of the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cuppings of the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the cupping does not draw blood, because of the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason one does not become faint, as when one makes a vein bleed;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, nor at all fire nor sense of fire, in any disease that comes from excess, as long as the whole body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to cup, or by habit, if we administer them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and within and at each time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they have a task of bloodletting, weigh heavily on the head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who experience a flow of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who faint, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the midst of the month, we command to wait for three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saliva of the mouth helps with the grief of the head … which comes to the eyes, and it is not suitable that it should be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this bloodletting is in the place of the saliva of the head, and it is not suitable for he who is of cold complexion in usage, or who has a catarrh, because it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and because of this it does not suit but the old man who uses it, nor those who have or catch cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often uses it, becomes oblique, and therefore it is suitable to put the cupping glass a little lower due to the doubt of obliqueness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation in the neck is in the place of the healthy head and of the basilica, and because of this it is worth to strengthen the foot, and to mend the channel of the arm, and to touch, and to replenish;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it does not suit to push strongly, for if it holds too firmly, then it causes obstruction or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilations of the ribs on the neck are worth pains in the head, and obstructions and migrations, and strangulations, and pains at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the healthy basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it suits that you instruct the healthy one to press his hand to put, so he does not cut the artery, and does not bring forth excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The breathings from below the jaw are valid for a disease of the mouth, and a corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the place of the healthy lips of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Here is the translation:
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The breathings from the thighs are worth as much as the three large veins of the arm, because they attract blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon to not make a wound too deep, because the leg is nourished by flesh, and it knows beneath the nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping that is on the buttock is worth as much as hemorrhoids of the fundament, and similar diseases beneath, and it is necessary that the cupping be large, and be of a certain quality, so that it may well treat.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it was subtle, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and they make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses on the legs open wide, for they attract blood from all over the body, and alleviate ancient pains of the kidneys, and of the liver, and of the bladder, and restore the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in the place of two sponges, and of two clamps, and always they weaken the body after long use, and cause swelling to come in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cup is that you put it on empty, and suck at once, and put it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not cease from doing so, until you see the place red and swollen, and feel the flow of blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then fire, and reapply the cupping glasses, and take heed of the disposition of the body, for there are those who have such a tender skin, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to cauterize only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deeply.
et suce legierement.	and to suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to cauterize twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtly open the way of the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the wound is very deep, it is necessary to cauterize a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, then we suffice only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, then we repeat often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the wound is deep, then we cauterize deeply, and the terminations are such that the heart should be perceived suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have strangled pores, that you apply the keys of opening oil, apt and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in this state, of violet oil, or of almond sweet oil, or of oil from cucumber seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in ivy, of oil from cress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balsamite, or oil of aniseed, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one has delicate skin and large pores, it is not necessary to apply oil, but rather wash with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, take away the essence of ivy, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities lift with old wine, or with water of elder, or with a decoction of nettle or of chamomile, or with other similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not advisable to apply a cupping glass before the bath, but after the bath, an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he should be warned, when he must be cupped and when he is being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are being bled, for they are choleric, and if their blood is too agitated and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary to take cold things, such as apples, grapes, and lettuce in the basket, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mild poultices, and flesh of capon, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, takes syrup of honey, and fragrant wine moderately, which is between old and new, and mild poultice, and mild poultices and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will be bled, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some men three or four draughts of triacle or muscat before bleeding, or afterwards, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be subtly purified, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The bleedings that are applied without hurting are those that are applied to the liver, and to the spleen, and to the podagra, and to the belly and the bowels and the loins and the thighs, for these members do not suffer from being hurt on the skin, and one does not do it except to attract blood from member to member, as we put them on the arms when the veins are healthy;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To open the viscosity which is in the limb, as we put ventoses on the belly and on the thigh to reduce the swelling of the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is opilation or stone, if remove by its attractive virtue by chance the opilation, or dislodge the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one puts it on the hollow and on the thigh when there is retained viscosity, and these ventoses are administered empty to suck out so much moisture;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain hot water is used, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the ventouse with warm hot water or hot water in which herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping administered by fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half palm widths from the fontanel, and it has a small hole on the side of the millet, just as if to push in a needle, and be careful beforehand lest you prick the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have in hand a rod of across iron or steel, to put a clamp in place, and be they great and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the blisters of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin than of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should one then put this blister on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the clamp of wax or linen, and put it in the blister across the rod that is in the blister, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the blister so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and hold it in place with two strips that we have mentioned, so that when one wants to, the vapors go out, and remove the blister;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the linen as before, and reapply it often, if you have mastery.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, to every ache, there is no vein nor perforation, and it is not administered unless when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only slightly;
et c’est li forme:	and that's its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without them being administered unless in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, like eyelids and cheeks, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in naked parts of the body, such as fingers or toes, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the usage is that when you find cuppings that are in soft, clean, and sensitive places without pore, if you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a soft and gentle manner, so they become familiar, and have nothing in the way of wind;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be healed of vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put on the bandages;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full, and attract, it is whether there or one can put a cupping, if he puts, for it is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the lever of axle, and then of water, very well, and then sprinkle;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the levers are too close to the body of the bandages, then wet the linen cloth in cold water, and put on, until the wounds are strengthened;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds are multiple, then put on a glassy paste, or wafers, and similar things, until they are strengthened;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the lever a poultice of peas, and let them stay until they adhere to the lever, then it will staunch now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more of this craft, take other sinews.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the sinews do not want to take, rub the joint with fresh blood, or stick an needle in so the sinew takes it, and then put them back, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will become firm.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they adhere, sprinkle on a little of aloe and of sieved powder, or of ash, so they will cling now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish wise men of this chapter do not find anything in the ancient books, nor did they read any letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason is estranged the knowledge in our land, because I did not find any good in it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except by the knowledge of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the knowledge, and by experiment, and by the practice of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where the wise men place their understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who have experienced it know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or twist or fracture occurs, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, so that nothing harms them completely, just like weakness of body, or infants, or old people.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the tendons are not very strong, or too fragile;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid eating cold joints, that is to say frozen meats, and meat of goose and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat raw fish, and do not overfill with foods that fill the veins with blood, lest you have doubts about a hot abscess, or expansion of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if he examines the patient at their first governance that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or they have viscosity, just as if they were cooking in water, and rice, and bread, and feet, and stomach of a calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a broken nose, representation makes sores and most quickly the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well reset or rejoined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, like the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but it is not a remedy, to reset the broken bone in the large tendons which are hurt and join the limb together, so that it becomes strong as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not to burden him with all points of his work, and therefore he must be nourished with thick broths, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	Because the break of the head is different from the break of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the elbow, and another in bending, as when one holds a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it breaks with a wound, and breaks into a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in each manner he has his engine, and his proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes into his place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the breaking of the bone is through that which the joints are twisted, and appears well by swelling, and sounds to the pressing of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting in his touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no point of breakage;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or crack, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not want to move your hand, but rather apply medicines that come hereafter, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breakage which goes into the joint, and are the two disjointed parts, they must now be set in equal alignment, so that abscesses do not gather there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses gather there, let it be for a day, as long as the abscesses are appeased;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it in a position where you can lift lightly and knowingly, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restorations of that which has pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then restrain it, as it must be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, whether it is of two parts, it is hand or foot, or to your hand if it is small members, or to two strings, or to a string and to your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are reassembled, you reset by adjusting all the additions in their proper places, and take care that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust the two heads of the bones according to their best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who come to make an abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, gently chastise the patient so they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, or turning, or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is so well secured that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not at all points, and it is necessary to put him in such a disposition that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him straight, so that twisting does not come when he is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Here is the translation:
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to envelop with gentle and subtle wraps;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to envelop with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large limb, and hold it steady on all sides equally, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then one puts light stuffing, three or four according to the limb, and holds the hand a little at all the bandage, then goes above the fracture and holds it less, so that the fracture then slowly releases the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the little finger a little at a time, until you grasp a large part of the whole sound limb, then take the other finger, and turn it back again around the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break, and hold it moderately, not too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first rule above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the swollen fingers linen or cloth strips, until it is all even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made stitches on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is inflammation or abscess, then put on something that appeases the hot abscess, and which reduces the inflammation, and let it be so for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then hold with your stitches, and make a splint of a large cane rod straightening, or of wood where they make the cleats, or of palm branches, and adjust according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the staple which one places on the fracture be a little bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as it needs to fit the member's smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold steady against the staples just as you did at the first dressing, then tie above a thread conveniently, just as at the first dressing on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the more tightly it is held, so much the less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, just as I have seen the works of foolish people who make their ligatures with twisted flax cords, and it's a great error, for the dressing cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that there be less than two fingers' breadth between each staple.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the heads of the stars after the straining in their sound limbs, then put beneath them poultices of linen, or a piece of flesh, so that they do not become bruised.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the course is broken, I will tell you the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And beware that it is not suitable to strain the stars (joints) all at once, lest the broken limbs be injured further on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it does not need to be touched with these forces until five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the post-operative swelling that suddenly occurs.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see in this way the method of the ancient plasterers to restore fracture, dislocation, and twist:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that holds itself as walls of the mill, and knead it with abundant water, and make this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and it's the common method of the plasterer restoring fractures in many dispositions, and even for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plastering that restores fracture and dislocation and twist:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take abrasives and lanolin and enula and asafoetida and Arabic gum and myrrh, in this proportion;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	mirror and balms, anoint with;
alechil VIIII З.;	oil of VIII;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make powder, and mix with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is warm, thus use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of plaster that is valuable for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugwort and wiszmelve, anoint with X;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	mirror and balms, anoint with VIII;
acaice VI З.;	acacia VI;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	armenic bolus X, and crush well, and mix with water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and alleviates the severe pain, and reduces the swelling of the bone, and the fracture:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take a new lancet, and the embers in ash and oil, and place on the patient's body.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore at first, but they are good for easing hot abscesses, and properly relieving the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to treat fractures that restores broken bones:
