pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves, and earthy peony leaves, and crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat for the restoration of the bone fracture and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of violets, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of oats, each a part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and crush, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are inflamed, mix with moist coriander water, or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat more forcefully than the first, when an abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of violets, and seed of flax, balusta, melilot, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each a part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crush, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a broken limb for restoration more than a certain amount of wax and oil, and nothing else besides, and says it should be between two extremes, not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one should apply warm dry cupping to the broken member, to restore it, with slightly hot things, like mirrors and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of plastering that is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and herbs of decocted omes, or pens of bird's wings, and visnaga, and equalize them, and crush them, and make a plaster and apply it to the location.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then lift it up a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone out of its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not lift it up with gentle hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the location, or swelling, without rest or inflammation, if you hurry, and lift it up, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light drapery, and a sea sponge moistened, and dip it in water, and lift up the location, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is alleviated;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then place it on a dry linen cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, and tie it with a bandage, so that you are certain of a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then resume the subtle treatment, and a little bit of emplaster, and do not strain it so strongly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and subtly treat it until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has cooled and reduced and pain and swelling are gone from everything, and you have mastery of emplastering and bandaging, then restart it, just as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if it does not come to the member any of what we have said, do not dislocate it further until after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the breakage is evident, and approach the adjustment of the flesh above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than at first, and let its flesh grow, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the dry limb more than a master is not, know that no nourishment can come to it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply the warm water therapy, every time you dislocate it, and let it be each third day, and ease the ligament a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	through this work then correct the nourishment to the limb, and quickly mend what makes the foolish mirror, which restores the twisted limb:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad, and if it is a painful work, and I do not see anything else but to soothe the pain and to open it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, and diverse shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a spear, and the neck of the bone breaks all the way to the underlying bone, as if it were shattered or crushed;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and because of this it is called this type of bruising "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the spearhead cuts through the bone from above, sense piercing, and is called this type of bruising "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and it is the wound of these two large or small bruises.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fissure or break in the neck of the stone, or fall on the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a persistent bruise, which approaches just near the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this is the wound whether large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is implanted in the bone as subtly as a goat's hair, and it is the small fissure, and because of this it is called this bruising "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound that is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and makes the piece of bone go down, and it is like the joints are when they make them warm, as the braziers do when they strike on the braziers;
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the bone within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have a moist head of bone, like the head of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and there are all these ways of breaking where small fragments are dislodged as if they were shattered.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all ways of breaks by the subtraction from them, and the inquiry with tension, and by the corrupt flesh that is on.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of the hairline is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone, and one rubs against it, then the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the break, beware of these accidents that harm the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and numbness, and ague fever, and the eyes issue forth and redden, and other similar things in worse dispositions, so that one cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an accidental wound, and you expect healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nave comes to you first, and it is winter, then you should open the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to open the bone before the seventh day, so that the membrane under the bone does not become corrupted, and come the accidents that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the breakage of the bone reaches just to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you mend the fractured part in this way:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take hold of the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and according to the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if a flow of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess bursts, it is with the help of what is necessary, and it is that you fill the hole with soft medicated drapes soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the bursting abscess is calmed, and be assured of a flow of blood.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin within the bone to open, and it is done according to two manners of work.
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner is that you cut at the narrow tail end beforehand, and it is the shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another larger cutting instrument than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have a number of diverse cuttings, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are of iron indeed.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly, so you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce within, in such a way that you do not administer cuttings with tareres, nor make them too deep lest they penetrate beyond the bone of the thigh, and should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass out of the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have more, if each one returns to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have tareres throughout the entire test.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and it's the form of the three manners of scarifications:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality to perceive through the broken bone is that you put the scarification on the bone, and turn to your fingers as much as you know that the bone is perceived;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the scarification elsewhere a little after, and thus do it all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the parts, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have as if grasping, pinching;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the vital spirit.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have perceived the bone and drawn it out, it is fitting that you reassemble the apartness which was separated from the bone to all the other instrument similar to an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more tenuous and more subtle than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it remains none of the small bones, no nails, if they lightly touch one of the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then heal the wound with tents and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of surgery is that which Galen described, which is more safe;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and it holds very firmly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, there where the break appears, so when you have discovered that part, then put below the head of this curved incision, which is its form.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side, and the affected part is on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently shape the entire bone around, and be very careful of the membrane that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is close to the bone, shape it lightly, for one shapes it well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is covered so much by above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to clear the scales with a subtle rasp, which you must have in different quantities, to prepare each location most conveniently, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you rasp with large rasps, and then with more subtle ones, and do not cease from doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-like fractures and subtle breaks, you must adjust the cause according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and it is a thing that is not readily responded to by one who has placed their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the swelling is discovered, it is necessary that you take a bandage of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another doubled bandage in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first bandage;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and make it lighter than you can, so that you do not irritate the swelling, then administer from above another string, and do not constrict it further than necessary to hold the wound sufficiently;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be thus for a day or two, until the heat of the abscess is alleviated, then disbandage it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of vegetables, and powder of incense, and aristologe, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put on the wound, and immediately administer Mondelfian's medicine without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is immediately clean, so you do not leave it to suppurate, nor allow it to gather in a lump, for when the lump gathers on the membrane of the brain, it corrodes and putrefies, and brings great evil to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts on the wound a biting medicine, it pierces through above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take warnings therefore, no bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackening comes from the medicine that one has put on, which has such virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix in the glue, and put it on the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound with various kinds of cures that are necessary, until it be sound.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that some times the two parts of the nose are broken above, or one by the sole, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the cartilage beneath is not broken, if it does not make a false swelling or twisting, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must put your little finger or instrument into the nose, and match the break equally with your index finger, and by gentle pressure, so that the nose regains its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the finger, and cannot be brought to the joint, it is necessary that you put it equally at the head of a thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is of two parts, do it similarly, and hasten to restore on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscessed swelling is appeased, then apply to the head of the nose tenderly with a strip of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you break one, another breaks instead;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the sutures be so large that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they direct any restorer that one must soften the tents in burr, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that it is good, but rather they should be softened with a concoction of egg white and powdered millstone;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the suture, until the bone is firm, and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And no one should put onions or eyes of garlic in place of sutures, and if there is a sweet dressing on top, and it holds the breakage, and soothes the patient within;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And abscesses that come to the nose while you are operating, if you put cerotate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a poultice of dyaculum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if apostemes (abscesses) come, apply an emplaster made from flour of sisament, and powder of incense, mixed with egg white, then put on light poultices, and do not bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break is small, and it breaks into minor pieces, then it needs suitable instruments to reset it, afterwards sew up the gash, and cure things that are bitter and harsh, suddenly, as we apply suitable plasters and ointments to it.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no inner wound in the broken limb, then the treatment of tendons, and I put bandages of plaster, until it be healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated, and there is no point of injury outside, and the break is outside so much, and it is not broken in two, except that a little lump forms inside, if one recognizes it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you put your right index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the break is in the left jawbone, then put your right index finger, and gently adjust the break from within, and hold it with the other hand by force, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is dislocated inwardly, it is necessary that you administer extension of the jaw in that part, so much that it becomes even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth are dislocated, or loose, then hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put on the broken jawbone a cerote, and put on a double bandage.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place on the drapeau a large well-made staple, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and lay it on the mouth that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure changes, then dislocate it again on the third day, and then put back in place what is dislocated;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster there, of powder from the mill with abundance of egg white or flour of sediment, after that you have removed the crust;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and apply a light plaster there, and if the plasters stick, and the patient's condition does not change, let it be until they are healthy;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times it is healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses or ulcers come, so manage them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reset the null piece of bone that was dislocated;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of the ostrum removes cumbersome obstructions from it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is constricted, so enlarge it with a flame according to the need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have gathered all these pieces, and there remains none, if the wound is large, and put on it suitable dressings to heal the flesh, so that it may be healthy.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture breaks many times beforehand, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and disarticulated into two, and there are pieces, and it is easier to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the operations are when the break is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one touches the shoulder where it feels the broken fracture;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches out the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put the break in alignment with your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have need to extend further, then put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or of wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And stand upright with strength, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you put evenness on the fracture, as it is necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot straighten the head of the fracture at the back, because it comes in front, it is necessary that the patient leans on his shoulder, and put underneath the shoulder a soft cushion, and bend the ministers below the shoulder, until the bone of the fracture is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then reduce the fracture to your fingers, and if you find fragmented pieces, it is necessary that you sew them together;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any prominence, it is necessary to cut to one of the incisors that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but you put beneath the strength this instrument, to guard against the swelling;
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not a cheesecloth, and be as wide as the bone requires, according to the size of the bone and the power of the instrument;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two instruments, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, according to the routing of the wound that you made when you drew out the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, if the wound is small, or you doubt it's a hot abscess, then fill the wound with dressings and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the hot abscesses come, apply a dressing with rose oil and in vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The straining of the bone, when it is without wounds and without injury, is that you put on the bone a plaster made of millet powder and egg whites, and apply light poultices, and put a splint underneath, if you are skilled in this.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage of a palm's length, then put a double layer of dressing on top of the poultices, and the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a subtle stick of three fingers' width and length, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and apply the staple to the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and underneath the healthy joint, and underneath the sick joint;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and the reset of each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture firmly, and you clearly see that the staple does not move on the broken bone, if you reward it every day, and when the ligaments relax, if you restrain it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient sit on his back, and place him when he sleeps in a small pillow underneath the joint, to lift the shoulder high;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if you alleviate the fracture of the forearm by aligning the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not dislocate it again with bad accidents, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then resume the dressing, if you see that it is necessary, and restrain it and leave it thus, until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored to the best within 28 days, and in less than any other remedy.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Because the shoulder breaks or dislocates easily when not in its proper place, and one cannot set it right except by touching.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you adjust according to the shape of the break, and reset according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the limb powdered with mill dust along with abundant egg white, and light bandages, and put on a double layer of cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a sturdy and subtle stick, a little larger than the shoulder, and so arrange the stick that it does not bump into any part of the shoulder, if you fill in with a layer of linen bandages, so that the stick is held evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it all together with a strong bandage firmly, so that the stick does not move from its place, and examine the ligament every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time he anoints, if he holds steady, and puts equal the handle so it is far from its place, and guides the patient on his side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is accomplished, if you disjoin, and be careful, for it's not the bone that sets in place lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone protrudes beforehand, and not beneath the heart, if it swells up, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the force to appease an abscess hotly.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is never broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken within, it declines to the underside, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks alignment, and suffers, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the fractures in the broken bone, and the sensation is not good.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient guides himself on his back, and you put a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the sides of the two ribs with your hands, and subtly adjust to put equal in all the ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then put them on emplaisters and stoups above the subtle star of salt, or another light fusion, and envelop it in a drapil, and bind it to the broken bone, so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the round ligament to the back, and hold it firmly, and reward each hour the treatment, and if it relapses, then hold it firmly.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it wants to dislocate, due to corrosion or prickling that comes to the joint, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and dislocate, and scrape off the emplaister, and address what has come from various methods of cures.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the emplaister, and hold it steady until it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the fracture of the ribs does not come forth unless in large lumps after the back, and inside the head, and do not plead unless because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and he feels well at the inquiry of the two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatments are that you make the break even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a bandage, so you have mastery over it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels very great pain, and puncturing, just like in pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it reaches a point, and all and vomits greatly of blood, and this is a grievous wound, and the old men have put great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that they can administer foods that inflate the belly, to soften the fracture by breaking.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, because hot abscesses do not come to life, if they have not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has arrived, then it is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that some of those whose veins are opened on the back, to suck out strongly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt that the veins do not attract the superfluities on the back due to the weakness of its disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And one must cover the limb with a warm oil in a hot bath, and place tents between the ribs to adjust the ligature inside, then it is cured of the treatment of pleurisy, of food and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the bone that pierces the membrane, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to open on the back of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath an instrument to protect the fragile area;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut into the bone, and treat lightly, and then cauterize the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and apply a poultice, until he is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses come, put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and apply them to the affected area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat thus the affected area with what is needed to bring about an abscess, and apply poultices soothingly on the painful side where it ought, until he is healthy.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes at the neck of the collar bone, and soon after, it happens that it breaks;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortally wounded in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when one holds them firmly and steadily, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient's injuries are cured, so one may put a cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, take heed if the feet are numb, and if the accidents that are in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary evacuation;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has been sewn onto his belly, if it bursts with a sudden movement.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is swooning on his back and wants to settle, it cannot happen.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not labor in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, it is the thing most lightly.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you warm it if there is a hot abscess, apply to the spine oil of rose or oil of May dew, so that it be appeased;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply to one of the comforting and drying plaisters, and bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until it be healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes disjointed, it is necessary to cover over the heart;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and reset the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then apply a treatment of ointment, softening the flesh, until it be healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the knee", you should put your pouchet in your left hand, and hold it evenly with your other hand at your power, then apply the plaster and the staple above, so you have mastery;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then hold it straight, and if there is a broken bone, fix it above, and the bone, and heal the wound until it is healthy.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Because it happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it happens, there is not much loss of amenity at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and make a long splint, and adjust it to the patient, and comes to the painful spot on the limb, and punctures, and inflames what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, so that you are above the breakage;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and he knows what is the fracture and the shape of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is in the head solely, set the fracture equally, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is too long, or it declines inward, then make the patient sit on their belly, so that the restoration of this fracture may be facilitated.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it equally, put it on the plaster, then put it on a straight stick or beam, and hold the fracture steady, so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the poultice beneath the ribs, until the binding is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a abscess forms there, do not touch it, until the abscess is appeased, and put on what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, so that there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	and that's the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joints are those which are between the rib and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods.
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	where one is to take the full plain of the grinder, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And lay the chains on the links, and they are raised high, and thus the patient is seated;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then he throws his broken arm on the log, until it comes to the notch, and has in the middle of a curve of wood, then hangs on some heavy thing or the ministers extend downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the mirrors to the fracture equal with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his haunteril, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands the ministers that one should hold what is on the breakage with his hands, and the others should hold underneath all the joints, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too forceful, hold the ligature below the breakage, and above the breakage, and extend each of the ministrations to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it should be that you place the soft lien underneath the notch, and another towards the cot, underneath the fracture;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the cot, it should be to place the lien lightly, without pressure, until the fracture is even on the limb, and on the cot;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set equal the fracture, as it is necessary, and hold steady, so that abscesses do not form there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses form there, do not hold steady less than seven days, and put on a soft cloth in vinegar and rose oil, until the abscesses are softened.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold steady, and the manner of holding steady is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm at the joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage, and hold steady at the joint, and on the arm, so that the arm is in a straight line, nothing disturbs it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use a straight line, and put on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers from each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then hold steady on the stiles, thus as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, more strongly and less in aligning.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the stiles, and the holding steady, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it stay tied up to seven days, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look for three days at the bond, that it does not swell in life, or the nourishments cannot come to the limb because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you hasten, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, then do not untie it sooner than after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and put his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the shoulder a cushion full of wool, equally thick, and look every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not move, nor are the bonds loosened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If you advise through the power of medicine, and give the meat that we have presented beforehand, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg are taken in hand for 40 days of entire treatment;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must dislocate and administer baths and medicines of ointments to comfort the injured place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is lazy and numb, it delays loosening for 10 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two twin" ones, where one is small, and it is the one that joins the wrist.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is underneath, towards the little finger.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	perhaps the large "foscile" bone breaks solely, or the small one, and perhaps they break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small fractures are broken, the restorations are light, and the healings;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and worse than when they are broken and put together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's a small fracture that is slightly broken, then one must extend it lightly, and set it evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's a large fracture, it needs to be pulled stronger;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it on the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so the patient does not suffer any strain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then stretch out the ministrations like arms to the part below his hand, or at the wrist, and another ministration to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts his mirrors equal, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it's a break in pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is no disordered part that can be grasped by the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make it like the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	Take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration a suppurating abscess occurs, apply a poultice made from rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and apply the poultice subtly above, until the suppurating abscess is alleviated.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax, and put on an emplaster of powdered millet with plenty of egg white, then apply the staves, and let the stave of the fracture be a little stronger, and a bit larger than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it should have six staves or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold more firmly on the fracture than other parts, and tighten less as you go further away, just as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages be those that are on the fragile and moist areas, and not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, from which it is strained, be of linen, not too large nor too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And rewrap the limb and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, as if a prick occurs which comes to the limb, then it is necessary that you apply warm water to the limb, until the pricks are soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be restricted from resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the bandaging, and if the ligaments are weakened and the bones disarticulated, and similar things, adjust them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take heed that the nourishments cannot come to the limb, because it is too constricted, it is necessary that you soften them a little, and let thus some hours pass, until the nourishments can flow in, and then strap it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not unwrap it for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	where he turns inward, then he bends his hands to his neck, and his neck is even, and beware of movement and jerking, and sleeps on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Here is the translation:
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or sprained, it is necessary that the patient's arm be crossed, and straightened directly in front of him evenly.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then put his hand on the stretched-out toe, and stretch out the ministers the broken bones, and put them in their proper places, so they are well-jointed.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and the bandages, lest abscesses come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the injury.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is in the palm of the hand towards the belly of the plant, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken hand.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then bind with a long bandage, and let the splint be of soft leather as big as the plant of the hand, and bind it, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is in the finger, it is necessary that you put a staple above, and another below in the palm, so that the hand is covered and straight, then bind everything together around the hand, and tighten the bandage between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the break comes to one of our fingers, it is the puffed up part, set it even, as it should be.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and hold with the sole of the foot, and if you see that you put a small straight steel bar to lift the break, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the break is in other fingers, like in the index finger or one of the others, set it even, and bind it with the healthy finger that comes after.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	where you bind them together in a holding position, which is worth more, or you put on a steel bar, as if in a puffed up state.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the disposal of hot abscesses, and suck out what comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is often broken, and one clearly sees this when it turns in front and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is when one lays the bandage on the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	The patient puts it on his face, then each minister stretches out his bandage to its equal part;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and it's when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the hip, so be one of the ligaments towards the thumb, and the other ligaments beneath the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And thus it's near the knee, and then the bandages are below the knee, and so is the extension downwards;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the mirrors to the bone equally with his two hands, so it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and there, where the abscesses come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down, then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The treatment is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture with a doubled bandage in two or three layers, and removing the superfluity, then twist the leg so that the heels come to the root of the nail, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread above;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put on the bruise these, and put a staple on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make equal the constriction, then begin to bind firmly in three turns or four on the bruise;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and when you go further above the bruise, and loosen less;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then you have two heads of thread that you had placed between the leg and the thigh, and bind three of these which are above, then return to the underside at the head of the thread, until you come to the bottom of the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and constrain it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that neither an abscess nor a swelling nor another similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, if he dislocates, and adjust what comes next, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that prick, one must extract them, it is possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, one must break the bone and make a fracture;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and the treatment is as we have said, until he is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the hip joint is broken in this way, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	in any case, in the restoration made thus, it does not bother the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is known that the pulse is restored at the same hour, or almost less or almost more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the gutter of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groove of the knee joint there is little bruising, but it often bursts.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it's not just a crack, or a perforation, and it has to do with the whole wound, and feels wounded, and this senses a great pain.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one puts back in place what is broken at its joints, until it is assembled as well as one can.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then put on the plaster, and you put a round stave, if you have mastered it, and hold steady as it should be held, then reward all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "tibia" by right and the other is called "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and there is a similar fracture as it comes to the arm, and therefore the restoration is like that of the equal arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns entirely aside.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it is clearly seen.
et torne desoz.	and it turns awry.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then administer extension, and set it equal, and lay the staples equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but always, it is necessary that the break be gentle, and there are many pieces, so that the extension should be less and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and adjust according to its strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completely finished your work, take two wooden skewers that penetrate the leg on both sides, and are as long as the leg from the knee to the ankle.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap it in two leaves of bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle, and at this binding the leg cannot incline to the right or to the left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and anyone who administers the wooden skewers as long as the leg, and it is of wood, and they put it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly done, it is in the fracture or where there is a wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and examine the leg each day, to see if there is a hot abscess or another accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you treat it until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the villa, there is no break, but the bones in the foot sometimes break and sometimes two pieces, and it does not happen that they are shattered in many dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens that the bone of the foot is broken, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then now put your foot on the shin, where the bones are lifted, then press until they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.
